defence peace lately tranſlated laten englyſſhe ¶ kynges moſte gracyous priuilege excellent noble warke whiche author therof hath entytled defender maynteyner peace becauſe doth moſte perfectlye treate clearely dyſcuſſe queſtyon aboute great controuerſy contencyon hath ben nowe longe tyme aſwell iuſte power auctoryte emperour vſurped power byſſhop rome otherwyſe called pope worke profytable dyuynes laweyers generally thoſe whiche louen exercyſen ſtudye good letter learnynge whiche ſayde worke wryten made two hondred yeres ago vnto lodo wyke ceſar whiche came lynage moſt noble famyly kynred duke bauary nowe fyrſte imprynted publyſſhed ſent forth abrode englyſſhe tonge wyllyam marſhall ¶ louer trouthe ſpeketh boke go forth boke good men gladly ſhall reteyne louynge embraſynges tourne ofte hande whoſe mynde fyxed ryght trouthe maynteyne wronge falſehod ſtyfly withſtande thoſe perſones waraunt aſwell pleaſed ſhall wood rome ſhall grunte rubbynge gall ¶ tranſlatour reader good gentle reader haſt thou boke intytled latyne defenſorium pacis englyſſhe defence tuicyon mayntenaunce peace vndoubtedly full worthy ſo called ye thynge ſelfe vſe therof ſhall full well manyfeſtly declare ſhewe aboue two hondred yeres paſſed varyaunce ſtryfe controuerſy betwyxte proude byſſhoppes rome ihon̄ ye xxii benedicte xii clement vi moſt gentle prynce emperour lewes bauary byſſhoppes rome auncyent hyſtoryes make mēcyon cōmenly parte tyme yea euer ſyns haue ben ſtoute ſtubbourne proude preſumptuous vſurpers murtherers traytours rebellyons cōtrary theyr allegyaunces onely agaynſt theyr owne naturall ſoueraygnes lordes pryncꝭ kyngꝭ emperours alſo agaynſt prynces peraduenture without aydes conſentꝭ mocyons coūſaylles foreyn ſtraunge byſſhoppes nowe becauſe good emperour lewes moued leſſe pyte towardes louyng ſubiectꝭ true loue zele towardes worde god moſte godly honour wolde permyt ſuffre ſayd byſſhops rome conſume waſt deuoure ye accuſtomed maner theyr wycked vngracyous predeceſſours therfore ſaye aroſe betwyxte ſayd emperoure ſayd byſſhops greuous intollerable tragedy defence moſte iuſte cauſe whoſe imperyall maieſty lyked noble vertuous clerke marſilius padway compyle endyte ſame defence peace nowe touchynge ye tranſlacyon marſilius laten teachynge hym ſpeake englyſſhe beynge italyan whether done ſo well myght ſhulde haue ben woll ſaye hertely pray gentle reader take good parte correcte amende nede dyſprayſe doyng iugde hygh poynt learnynge tranſlate meanely thynke ſome learnynge dare bolde ſay iniuſt lyenge carpours pryuy detractours cōmeth nothynge lyght neyther preachyng ne yet wrytyng yt ſauoureth hath taſte vertue learnynge wolde gladly ſuche whyſperers blower mēnes eares wolde preache wryte ſette forth ſermons bokes vertue good learnynge ſame aſwell without makynge fayned vntrue eſcuſes without theyr olde accuſtomed crafty iugglynges truly declare publyſſhe worde god ſhewe themſelues ſuche theyr hertes ryght duety worde god ſhulde euer haue ben theyr mouthes theyr wrytinges theyr seales haue profeſſed ſworne olde prouerbe goldſmythes theyr owne occupacyons iniuſtly falſely ſecretly corner ſlaunder bely men nowe good gentle reader aduyſe counceyll woll ſelf ſay nothynge beleue theym ſoeuer ſay ſuche tyme vntyll haue done aboue ſayd alſo vntyl haue openly ſuffycyently improued confuted v make fewe wordes woll promyſe aſſure one thyng good reader admonyſſhe warne another ſo fare well boke dare ſaye thou ſhalte fynde wherwith make iuſte inuynſyble anſweres yea wherwith vtterly confute euery obieccyons fantaſtycall argumentes reaſons perſwaſyons papyſtycall ſorte made ſettynge forthe extollynge vſurped power auctoryte byſſhop rome ben neuer ſo falſe crafty ſubtyle warne tranſlacyon boke dyuerſe thynges ben omytted lefte mater ſo moche profytable longe tedyous laten boke large pleynly apperyth reſydue cō mytte thyne owne dylygence whiche readyng boke may nowyſe lacke thus farewell pray longe lyue proſperous preſeruacyon moſt gracyous ſoueraygne lorde kynge henry ye eyght moſt vertuous lady quene anne lady prynces elyzabeth doughter heyre theym bothe ¶ thus endyth preface tranſlator reader frendſhyppes ryches gyueth benefyces ryches gyueth power auctoryte ryches cauſeth regarded greatly eſtemed poore man neuer ſo good godly neuer ſo vertuous corrupte maners neuer ſo prudent wyſe lyeth euery wherein duſt yf ryche man ſpeake neuer ſo folyſſhely men magnyfie prayſe ſpeche ſayinge euen cloudes let poore man ſpeake neuer ſo wyſely man gyueth attendement hym dothe ſayinge mekenes humblenes lowlynes ſobrenes diſcrecyon good aduyſement ſoeuer nought ſet deſpyſed nowe dayes ſyde bolde preſumpcyon folyſſhe hardynes vnſhamefaſtnes aſmoche made meruaylouſly proſperous floryſſhynge trouthe ſoeuer nowe cōmen open hatred ſyde gloſynge flaterynge curryenge fauell pryncypally chyefly made pryce euer good mynde vertue leſſe cared thyrſte moſte peſtylent poyſonfull couetouſnes greater hygheſt loweſt greateſt ſmalleſt folowe couetouſnes nowe doth defende innocent man beynge weake feble iniury myghtye men great power iudge nowe dayes ſo vncorrupte loueth gyftes rewardes euer ſwerynge othes leſſe reuerence regarded periurye boldly vſed accompted ſmall none offence preuarycacyon playenge handes fraude gyle falſhed ſo great whiche gayly coloured paynted ſubtylite wyll ſay duplicite lawyer ſelues yf hope gylefull money glyſtre ſhyne lawes playnly beynge tourned mockage daylye made mockynge ſtockes tryfles money iudgement wry •• en wraſted made lytle worthe mocked deſpyſed luſte pleaſure euery lawyer pleder cauſes nowe dayes whiche ſueter lawe dye ſooner ſe ende ſuete oh theſe worſhypfull goodly lawes dede theſe excellent gaye place iudgement whiche ſuccoure pore wretch deſyrynge ayde helpe ſuche faſſhyon maner ben moche better haue loſte ſoeuer whiche haue begon ſuete lawe haue fallen ſo comberous endles labyrynthes maſes iudgementes whenſo waye gette agayne yf man one entrede forſothe haue ſeen ſelfe certayne men whiche haue ben lordes owner lytle money ſuche delay ſtayes ſtoppages made lawe broughte ſo great pouertye haue conſtrayned neceſſytie begge aſke theyr fode dore dore certayne ende theyr lyues hoſpytalles ſpytle howſes whiche began ſue trye lawe theyr poſſeſſyon ſubſtaūce worthe foure fyue thouſandes called decyde determyne cauſes ende ſuetes ſtryues prouyde laufully quyetnes profyte cytezens cōmynalte paſſyng ouer courtes place iudgement thynge beſyde ſobre meſurable dyſcrete belongynge temperaunce el accordynge equyte good conſcyence whiche nowe dayes exercyſe gyue mynde vnto euermore waſtfull exceſſe ſuperfluyte maner thynges couetouſnes feruent hote vngracyous wantonnes outrage fornycacyons adulteryes ſtyffe obſtynate pryde ſhameles ambycyon deſyre honour vaynegforye prayſe vnfaythfull falſe gyle deceyte lewde plēty open robberyes cruelty thryſte murther ſhedde man blode euer ye fury woodnes rage warres bataylles noyaunce myſcheuouſnes perelles daungers ſtronge preſent thynge chryſten reader thynkeſt thou ought blame ſo dyuerſe ſo manyfolde ſo contynuall t̄reble thynges worlde deſpyſinge ſettynge nought godes worde cauſe ye preſent euylles ī worlde wherof iudgeſt thou belonge wherof el haue greuouſly offended hurte truthe goſpell truthe hated v whiche wolde accompted taken owne chyldren brone owne howſe hatefull barbarous hethen men neuer ſo cruell beaſtly auctoryte reputacyon trouth amonge v maieſty ſhe defende ſaue herſelfe nowe lenger nay rather thynge nowe dayes deſpyſed ſet nought thynge troden vnderfote haue quenched put lyghte world ourſelues yet meruayle yf lyke blynde beaſtes ſtumble fall euery euylles wretchednes yea ouer whiche greuous thynge many v onely ſtumblynge vtterly peryſſhynge lacke knowlege vnderſtandynge perceyue peryſſhe reioyce prowde hurtꝭ calamytes wrackes lykewyſe yf victory trouthe lyghte worlde ſayth chryſte ſoeuer foloweth walketh darknes beholde deſpyſe openly truthe whiche chryſte yet ron awayes forſakers truthe nothynge aſhamed pretende royally name chryſte callynge ourſelues chryſtyans yf chryſte truthe dede chryſten man profeſſyon dyſcyple truthe thynge myght trouthe teache owne ſelfe thynge coulde scoler learne hauynge trouthe teacher trouthe itſelfe conuenyent accordynge ſo maye fyre vnhote thynge whiche fyre hathe touched take heate waxe warme ſayde fyre chryſte moche trouth howe poſſyble hathe taughte dyſcyples trouthe therfore ſones men howe longe wyll heuy herted leauynge forſakynge trouthe folowynge mānes iudgement ſay vanyte leaſynge doctryne whiche trouthe folowyng blyſſed poore men ſpyryte theyres kyngdome heuens blyſſed meke perſones ſhall poſſeſſe erthe blyſſed whiche waylen mornen ſhall comforted blyſſed whiche hungren thyrſten ryghtwyſnes ſhall fylled blyſſed mercyfull perſones ſhall obteyne mercy blyſſed whiche clene herte ſhall ſe god blyſſed peaceable perſones ſhall called ſones god blyſſed whiche ſuffren perſecucyon ryghtwyſnes ſake belongeth kyngdom heuens theſe thynges ſeme v vtterly vnſauery el playne folyſſhenes dayes pore ſpyryte meke mercyfull peaceable innocent harmeles mowrne hungre thyrſte ryghtwyſnes ſuffre perſecucyon loue vſe theſe termes wordes ſtraunge vnwonte nowe dayes dothe nowe dayeshyſſe dothe ſtampe theſe thynges dreames madde men ſtarke folyſſhe tryfles ſay theſe wordꝭ latomus ſaye egmondamus ſaye hochſtratus whiche freres onely becauſe wyll name moſte holy father goddes vycars theſe moſte reuerende father hatted mytrede ſhall caſte forth beynge certayne ſuperſtycyous perſone heretyke turnynge ſayinge chryſte horne agaynſt go behynde v thou aduerſarye thou arte ſclaundre v beſeche loue truthe chryſten reader dothe trewe pouertye ſpyryte breathe nowe dayes ſheweth forthe lyuynge v dayes whiche rather ſwolne puffed vp ſpyryte owne wytte iudgement condempnynge comparyſon ſelues thoughe ſelues holy amonge v whiche yf neuer ſo lytle offended hurte mountenaunce one heare euen ſtarke woode madde angry wrothe neyghboure v dothe thyrſte greatly deſyre ryches honour pleaſures euen contumely reproche ryghtwyſnes man ſhall lyghtly fynde mercy pyte amonge v good ſmell ſwete ſauoure ſoyle durte myre praye v ſaye cleane herte dothe abhorre hate clennes herte gentyles hethen people olde tyme dyd hate vnlucky abhomynable augury yt ſay flyeng ſyngynge byrdes wherby betokened euyll happe myſchaunce folowe nowe place lefte lenger peace erthe ſhe vtterly exyled banyſſhed v nowe dothe ſuſteyne ſuffre euen leaſte dyſpleaſure euyl wyll man whiche power myghte ryghtwyſnes god rather whiche oureſelues trede vnder fote dothe ſuppreſſe dothe moche v lyeth quenche deſtroye ryghtwyſenes god myghte auaunce tere vp owne ryghtwyſenes myghte ſubiected apoſtle paule ſayth iuſtyce god yf thoſe afore reherſed thynges taughte chryſte whiche lyghte worlde doubte nyght hylles darkenes hathe taughte theſe thynges whiche diamerterly cleane contrarye thoſe therfore meruayle noueltye ſtraunge thynge yf ſuffre punyſſhement worthely deſpyſynge lyght goſpell yf daylye toſſed ſerably ſuffre ſhypwrake moſte thycke darkenes mēnes ſuperſtycyous worthely punyſſhed deſpyſynge lyghte goſpell moſte greuous tempeſtes ſtormes yf empoueryſſhed oppreſſed conſumed warres yf obſeſſed beſette compaſſed aboute euery ſyde roberyes yf vexed newe ſtraunge fylthye abhomynable ſyckeneſſes dyſeaſes ſuche hathe ben herde heretofore yf ſuffre great famyne hungre yf oppreſſed tyrauntes yf greatly troubled vexed monſters wonder yf noyed ſodayne incurſyons aſſautes wylde cruell beaſtes yf deſtroyed breakynge forthe floodes water yf ſwalowed conſumed gapynges openynges earthe fynally conclude whiche waye ſoeuer tourne iyes mynde ſhall ſe perceyue nothynge cruell noyſom hurtefull vengeable myſerable wretchedfull chylde wrangleth troubleth ſtryueth agaynſt aged man man lowe degree agaynſt noble man hygh eſtate degree thynges dyſparpled ſcatered thynges loſe theyr place thynges troubled ordre thynges lyke ſemen decay falle thynges whiche come hereafter feared without cauſe greuous dreadefull theſe whiche preſent ſuche paynes ſuche punyſſhementes ſuche vengeaunce dothe trouthe deſpyſed requyre done v ſuche plage requyren dyſcyplyne learnynge lyghte refuſed ſette noughte becauſe mocke ſcorne pouertye ſpyryte haue alſo nowe caſte awaye loſte hope promeſſe kyngdome heuens ſettynge herte deſyre vpon earthly thyngꝭ becauſe haue ceaſſed meke alſo nowe worthely ſo moche poſſeſſe earthe fyghte murthers cruell blody bataylles becauſe thyrſte vnryghtwyſenes nowe euery doo oppreſſe ryghtuouſe perſone therfore worthely throughe owne deſeruynge doo maner fynde token prynte iuſtyce remaynynge eche ouertourne deſtroye doynge iniuryes wronges one v becauſe refuſe forſake doynge mercye ſelues alſo ſomtyme worthely myſſe lacke ſame towarde v becauſe nowe embrace loue herte nothynge pure cleane accordynge deſeruynge alſo attayne gette moſte pure beame trouthe beynge cyrcūuented begyled falſhed lye fallen awaye vtterly faythe goſpell thynge beſeche good chryſten reader fall awaye goſpell vſe done dayly ſtede leuite ſoftnes gentylnes chryſte arrogancye preſumptuous pryde ſtede vertue good lyuynge vſe wantonnes hatrede ſtede charyte warre ſtede peace domynacyon rule lordſhyppe ſtede humblenes lowlynes vſurpe empyre hole worlde yet neuertheles notwithſtandynge ſtonde owne conceytes thynke ſelues haue ryght faythe chryſten lyuers dyd chryſte place teache earthely empyres lordſhyppes worlde coueted deſyred dyd teache rather maner wayes theſe thyngꝭ auoyded eſchewed doctryne euydent ſurely knowen haue ben perfectlye obſerued kepte true dyſcyples ſayde ſerue god alſo mammon ryches ſoeuer olde tyme dyd beleue hym duely oughte doo doubtynge nothynge thynge true theyr owne free wylles dyd forſake caſte theym theyr goodes poſſeſſyons beynge heuye wayghty burthayns ſo beynge lybertye lyghte folowed lorde lyfe whiche profeſſed theym ſelues guydes blynde perſones laughynge theym ſcorne theyr thus doynge whiche thynge moſte peryllous tyme dreade nothyng ſelues folowe phariſeys apoſtles ſayinge moſte expedyent chyefly profytable churche haue fatte ryche thynges rente profettes ſelfe craftely ſubtelly men churche dayes rather folowers phariſeys thē ye apoſtles pykynge gatherynge togyther holy scrypture fewe name ryche men whiche maye maner waye holde vp ſtrengthe maynteyne owne ſentence ſayinges paſſynge purpoſely none iyes faſte ſhytte cloſed wonte ſayde ſyxe hondreth place maketh contrary parte yet ſhall lytle dyuerſyte yf man wyll dylygentlye marke take hede betwene theyr maner rychenes oures fyrſte feare leaſte haue gotten ryches goodes lyke moche holylye ryghtfully abraham iſaach iacob iob ſuche dyd gette theyr ſubſtaūce whiche gatte whiche wayes laboures huſbondrye without hurtynge damagynge man v feare leſte haue made ſelfes ryche withoute paynes trauayle taken owne parte mēnes laboure ye oftentymes greefe ſmarte ſorowe alſo men beſyde thoſe afore reherſed perſones dyd neuer eſteme thyſe thynges ryches neyther whan plentyfull theym dyd ſette theyr herte vpon theym ſo doo whiche ſtryue kepe warre amonge ſelues one thyſe thynges fercely veray lyfe feare therfore ſaye leſte veray great dyuerſytie betwene theym v yf man wolde ponder dylygently conſydre maner gettynge vſe affeccyon bothe partes ſentence opynyon iudgement nothynge therfore holpen defended example deades theym whiche farre awaye elles couetouſnes wherby nowe gape gredely ryches theyr tyme worlde vnlyke farre awaye tyme worlde temperaunce meſurablenes contynency cleane lyuynge whan dyd ſo rage amonge ſelues murthers dayly ſlaughters thyſe thyngꝭ onely whan dydde vſe thyſe ryches goodes inſtrumentes benefycence lyberalytie euen towarde ſtraungers nacyons thoſe whome dydde knowe moſte cōmonly vſe theym helper aydes iniuryes wronges el exercyſe voluptuouſnes wantonnes whan dyd ſo haue theyr ryches accordynge ſayeng paule thoughe hadde theym contrary wyſe whan lyue ſo addicted vtterly gyuen bonde vnto ar founde perceyued poſſeſſed theym rather poſſeſſours bonde ſeruauntes vnto rather lordes mayſters theym ſo moche eſteme maner benefytes chryſte done v ſo great valure veray redy forgette theym cauſe loue wretched wycked māmone thyſe thynges odyouſe ſpoken odyouſe thyng thoſe thynges maye truely caſte agayne v layde charge truely auoyde theym clere ſelues theym thynke abraham wolde haue ben lothe euyll wyllynge haue loſte ryches neuer ſo great goddes ſake whoſe loue ſo well wyllynge content forgoo onely begotten ſone vndoutedly pleaſure ſubſtaunce worlde doo nowe folyſhly madly defēde couetouſnes example holy father whiche folyſſhely ſeche defence mayntenaunce couetouſnes example thoſe holye men lette v compare oure mynde theyr mynde towarde theſe fylthes lette v ſay yf ſhame v ſuche holy men ryche therfore lawfull v day nyght ryght wronge hoke croke clyme labour vp ryches example v ſo many ryche gaynefull benefyces whiche contynuelly meruaylouſe great care dylygence heape ſowdre togyther rome wolde contente forgoo lacke one halfe buſſhell beanes loue chryſte thoſe holy men wolde haue ſlayne euen theyr onely begotten ſones moſte obedyent mynde hope grace fauour byddynge forthwith without delaye forſoke theyr countre theyr kynſfolke clere contrarye cōmaundement couple ioyne togyther felde felde howſe howſe withoute meaſure ende haue gone ſo farre forwarde whiche pray god tourne good haue left narowe ſpaces rowmes leſſe landes lay men haue taken theym yet beſydes reſte afore flye vpon reſydewe alſo whiche lefte theym vntyll haue broughte people theyr wyfes chyldren ſeruytute bondage v whan ſhal haue done woll defende maynteyne haue ben done laufullye example abraham holy men lyke hym shall pray proper goodly comparyſon ſymylytude dyd thoſe men tyme take awaye wrongfullye mountenaunce one chekyn dayly becauſe owne profyte auauntage doo ouerthrowe deſtroye hole howſholdes yet neuertheleſſe couete accounted ſalte erthe full worthely forſothe comparyſon people chryſte many place denyeth dyſcyples elles hym ſelfe alſo worlde ſayinge theſe wordes yf worlde dothe hate knowe hathe hated afore yf ben worlde worlde truely wolde haue loued whiche belongynge ſelfe nowe becauſe worlde haue choſen worlde therfore worlde hateth beholde howe man chryſte hathe choſen ar world chryſt hath elected worlde therfore paule ſaythe yf dyd pleaſe worlde ſhulde ſeruaunte chryſte yet nowe fyghte maner armyes hooſtes worldlye domynyon rule none otherwyſe neyther lyghter faſſhyon dydde hethen men theyr lyfe tyme alexandre iulius name whome doo noo whytte refrayne yes meke accordynge chryſtes teachynge cōmaundement pore ſpyryte mercyfull hungre thyrſte ryghtwyſnes conſentynge agrement ſhortly thyne aduerſarye waye reſyſte euyll whan one ſtryketh ryght cheke holde forth alſo vnto hym thy lefte cheke yes ſaye whan one wyllynge take v coote delyuer vnto hym alſo gowne loue enemyes good whiche dothe hate v dare bolde denye chryſte taughte dyſcyples thyſe thynges maye ſo without moſte euydent cryme preuarycacyon manyfeſt praye knowen thoſe thynges may auoyde eſcape ſome crafte ſubtylyte ſay thyſe thynges vnderſtande thus lyterall grāmaticall cenſe ye moreouer fercely pronoūce hym herttyke forthwith ſoeuer ſhall iudge thynke true cenſe meanynge ſcrypture rather defended maynteyned coacte cenſe imagyned v affyrmynge oughte cleue leane expoſycion declaracyon holy father wytte dunce thomas sylneſter catharinus ſuche ſame ſorte seynge lawfull gyue credence ſcrypture hit ſelfe thyng muſt euery embrace cenſe whiche expoſytor maketh moſte true cenſe thynge pray compelled agaynſt wyl gyue credence men certayne veray tryflers gyue credence god nay rather thynge anulle make voyde lawe god bynde chryſten people luſt appetyte pleaſure man openly ſo fare behalfe thoughe churche coulde lenger knowe certayne goſpelles haue certayne apoſtels prophettes nowe wyckednes ſome men bolde affyrme ſay whiche thynke wykydneſſe ſome papyſtes abhomynable ſynne churche ſhuld haue ben moche better without goſpels therfore ben expedyent neyther ben wryten neyther receyued tyme tonge worthy tamed holden vndre brennynge fyre brymſtone chryſte ſayth apoſtels goynge worlde preache goſpell euery creature wycked man ſayth ben better goſpell neuer ben ſpronge vp ben begon gyue chriſte buffet blowe gyue chryſte buffet blowe vpon cheke thynge thynke man doubteth euydent men nothynge almoſte nowe lefte remaynyng holy ſcrypture whiche hath owne true naturall ꝓpre cenſe vnderſtandyng lefte ſaued hit ſelf haue wreſted applyed al thyngꝭ ye ſcrypture owne pompe ambycion owne power fede ſhepe folowe gyue thou beyng one cōuerted conferme ſtrength cōforte thy brother ii ſwerdes woll gyue ye key kyngdom heuens whatſoeuer thou ſhalt bynde vpon erth ſhall bounden alſo heuens c whiche thyſe ſayengꝭ nowe ſo applyed yt ſerueth rather ſenſual appetytes luſtꝭ intencion purpoſe chryſte albeit cenſe meanynge thyſe open veray manyfeſt clere perceyued ſeen euen blynde men yf man woll conſydre hole hyſtory goſpell yet neuertheleſſe contende ſaye ſtyfly ſo taken vnderſtanded ſhall moſte profyte make beſte purpoſe abuſe lyke maner v ſuffre nowe abyde thyſe ſentences folowyng otherwyſe vnderſtanded accordynge mynde pleaſure taketh owne croſſe foloweth worthy mete dyſcyple gather treaſures ſelues erthe theuys maye dygge moughtes wormes maye eate conſume prynces ruler gentyles vſeth domynyon ouer thoſe whiche greater exercyſeth power auctoryte vpon ſhall lyke caſe amonge ſoeuer wyllynge greater amonge lette hym mynyſter ſoeuer wyllynge chyefe amonge ſhall ſeruaunte euyn lykewyſe ſone man hathe cōmen mynyſtred vnto mynyſtre vnto wyſe thyſe ſentences fortyfie ſtrengthe prymacye auctorytie byſſhop rome byſſhop rome defende vnleſſe crafte ſubteltie ſo lay colour vpon couer ouer harde playſter kepe vnder truth may freely lybertie put forthe ſhewe ſelfe tyme el without ſhall appere clerely ſōne humylytie lowlynes cōmaunded chryſte v preſtes whan ſayth ſhall ſo amonge contrarye parte ſuperyoryte call bearynge rule vtterly forbydden thyſe wordes ſhall lordꝭ mayſters praye good reader attende take hede howe goodly thyſe thynges agre togyther amonge ſo kynges ruler gentyles vſe domynyon exercyſe auctoryte vpon theyr ſubgettes aſmoche ſaye beſeche thou peter thy ſucceſſours heyre euer empyre rome expoſycyon becauſe woll ſay thyng greuouſe worthy condempned prouerbe marked lytle rodde daſſhe made pen token dyſalowynge furthermore whiche foloweth cam mynyſtre mynyſtred vnto ſerue ſerued ye god wote aſmoche ſay emperours kynges rule earthe let fal downe theyr knee great veneracyon kyſſe fete adorned garnyſſhed precyouſe ſtones thy ſucceſſours ſyttynge ſolemply ſeate chayre aſtate gorgyouſe kynges ſeate moreouer ſayeng woll cheiffeſt amonge ſhall ſeruaunt wylleth greater amonge lette hym mynyſtre ſygnyfeyth betokeneth nothynge el onely haue power auctorytie cōmaunde reſydue churche muſte nedely obey peter yf thy mayſter meaned wordes dydeſt thou whan thou made chyefe capytayne hed thy bretherne ſaye thyſe wordes thyne owne ſelfe ſubgettes euery man loue god whether kynge excellent perſone duke perſones ſent hym certayne one moſte holy father greuouſly rebuketh ſayth lowde voyce thou peter dydeſt ſpeke thyſe wordes thy ſelf onely thy ſubgettes howe conuenyently metely hath founde ſtartynge hole helpe hym ſelfe ſhulde ſaye ſoeuer peter taughte dyd reache onely wordes dayes rather moche dyd teache workes deades contynuell example folowyng poynte alſo cuſtome maner mayſter chryſte euangelyſte luke ſayth iheſus began teache lykewyſe paule alſo ſayth folowers folower chryſte whiche cauſe ſame paule alſo cōmaundeth doer worker worde hym whiche onely hearer teacher excepte yt peraduēture beſemed peter teache onely ſo cuſtome begon brought vp hym becōmeth ſucceſſours ſame knowledge playnely ſuche dulnes wytte perceyue vnderſtande theologye dyuynyte beſyde dyd ye ſame peter go samarye iohn̄ ¶ nota peter cōmaūdemēt ye apoſtles went samaria whan bydden ſo apoſtels apoſtels aſſhamed abuſe prerogatyue prehemynence theyr hedde ruler mynyſterie ſeruyce pray doth hym ſelfe ſhewe forthe take vpon hym ſuche maner pretogatyue auctoryte dygnyte aboue epyſtles ſayinge one felowe byſſhops ſelfe equall beſeche byſſhoppes whiche amonge praye good reader canſt thou perceyue theſe wordes tutle poynte belongynge prymacye coulde ſpoken mekely lowlywyſe ſymplye playnly fyrſte callyng hym ſelfe felowe byſſhyp chalengeth hym ſelfe taketh vpon hym none excellence prehemynence aboue maketh hym ſelfe felowe lyke theym whan beſecheth ſo doynge chalengeth hym ſelf rule domynyon prymacye power auctoryte vpon forſoth yf woll herken gyue credence vnto peter paule hym ſelfe whiche ſpeake v holy ſcrypture god profyttes apoſtels rather owne dreames fantaſyes certaynly ſhall perceyue fynde call ſelues thynge el mynyſters theyr power noughte el mynyſterye hauynge theyr myndes farre awaye kynde ye apparaunce honoure onely ambycyons deſyre prymacye ſuperyoryte dothe lorde mayſter hym ſelfe often tymes reherſed ſay cōmen ſerued mynyſtre ſerue ſhall ſuffycyent ſeruaunt lorde mayſtre doth deſyre greatter mayſter nedeth make wordes ſcholyes gloſes cōmentes interpretacyons haue taken away wt gloſes wel nere dyuyne ſcrypture clene taken away deſtroyed well nere whole ſcrypture god srypture peraueuture ouertourned deſtroyed beynge dombe maner ſpeaketh neyther may vnder v tyrauntes may chylde whiche vnder rodde correccyon gouernour mayſter ſay nothynge onely whiche ſhalbe veray lykynge pleaſaunt v domynyons prymacyes chyefe ruler kyngdomes notwithſtandynge meane ſeaſon tryflynge vayne ymagynacyons fantaſyes taken awaye ſhe doth put v mynde remembraunce nothynge chyefly euery place ſhulde dyſpyſe ſet nought thyſe thyngꝭ cryeng playnly openly empyres ryches golde vyle ſtayle tranſytorye thynges peter ſayd symon magus enchauntour offerynge golde hym kepe thy golde thy ſelfe perdycyon wyſe man ſayth boke entyled eccleſiaſticus golde wood tree offenſyon wo whiche coueteth foloweth yet good lorde hokes wyles nettes make contyuually dayes catche ſo euyll myſcheuous thynge enterpryſe take hande boldely ſwyftly loue money power auctoryte place ſcrypture adulterate counterfeyte cortupte theſe fewe wordes lohere ii ſwerdes haue wrythen wreſted ſwerde empyre worlde emperours hande ſtoutely manfully god ſaue v chalenged churche albeit yt chryſte hym ſelfe doth ſay affyrme kyngdom worlde paule alſo ſworne oratour ambaſſadoure cryeth ſayeng wepons armour carnall ſtronge armour weapon ar carnal myghty god becauſe poynte boldnes preſumptuous pryde ſhulde wantynge v haue ſelues made foundament hed vnyuerſall churche hereof came vp thoſe ſtraunge name whiche olde tyme knowen thynge holy men generall vycar greateſt byſſhop many ſuche yet farre ſtraunge theſe whiche name dygnyte rede al peter epyſtles euer vſurped toke one hymſelfe paule knoweth hed churche onely chryſte make ourſelues hed bothe churche alſo empyre howe great tragedyes trouble haue cauſe rayſed vp hetherto churche howe many v haue ſtryuen lay maner emperours aboute name tytle longe hyſtorye reherſe amonge whiche emperours lodowyke iniuries contumelyes done pope rome lodowike bauarye emperour bauarye noble renōmed emperour beautye worſhyp moſte honourable ſtocke duke bauarye whiche inferyour none prynces tyme gentle courage mynde mercye pytie deuocyon holynes vertues vſed peace warre cōclude qualyties propertyes whiche cōmendable emperour whoſe defencyon haue put folowyng whiche wolde ſhuld beholden germayne borne rather nacyon ſo proudely preſumptuouſly handled entreated alſo ſo dyſpytefully cōtumelyouſly fyrſte iohn̄ xxii name benedicte xii laſt clement ſyxte beyng al thre byſſhops rome poſſyble haue hanled man prowde dyſpytefull maner greuous offence baptiſta egnatius hymſelfe alſo doth confeſſe albeit thynges wel nere great fauourer byſſhoppes rome onely durſte bolde take vpon hym name emperour without aſſent agremēt iohn̄ ſemed holynes byſſhop rome reaſonable cauſe ſuffycyent wherfore ſhuld onely interdicte ſo excellent ſo noble prynce sacramentes alldyuyne ſeruyce▪ • ut alſo denounce publyſſhe hym thoughe fautles heretyke preacher ſent forth brode hym al place ſame purpoſe moreouer entent purpoſe rayſe ſtyrre vp rebellyon ſubgettꝭ agaynſt hym dyd abſolue al yt ſworne hym maner othe whatſoeuer theyr ſayd othes theyr allegeaunce beſyde vexed hym warre bataylle choſynge cardynalles abbottes chyefe pryncypall capytaynes ſame cardynalles abbottꝭ capytaynes ī warre warre clement alſo dyd procure charles kynge boheme aduerſarye ſayd lodowyke named made emperour prynces electours ende ſo moch dyſcorde murther myght kendled amonge chryſten prynces whiche onely crafte ſubtyle practyſe wherby haue alwayes hytherto maynteyned thus theyr power auctoryte whiche hath cauſed ſo moche blode ſhedde ſo many loſe theyr lyues worlde yf vycar chryſte maye ſuche maners condycyons truely ſe maner tyraunte worlde may alſo vycar chryſte yf ought take vengeaūce yf ought praye euyn perſecutoures good alſo whiche hate hym yf ought refuſe exchewe erthely kyngdom yf ought abſteyne maner couetouſnes yf oughte walke ſpyryte fleſſhe ſe excedynge moche dyfference dyuerſyte betwene aforeſayd maners ordynaunce chryſt neyther vnknowen dyſpleaſure purchaſe myſelf whyles ſtyrre trouble pompe theyr abuſyon abhomynacyons meane ſeaſon farewel ſaye farewell ſoeuer ye thoughe preeſtes whoſe fauoure retayne excepte woll renounce forſake truthe whiche truthe itſelfe hath ſayd tolde worlde ſhulde come one brother ſhulde delyuer brother vnto deathe father ſone moreouer ſones ſhulde ryſe vp agaynſt theyr father put deathe farre awaye may ought frende man whiche hymſelfe frende truthe ought beleue man gyue place hym neuer ſo nere naturall kynne vnto neyther yet angell heuen yf preched thyng cōtrary angell beleued ſpekynge agaynſt goſpell goſpell seynge truthe whiche onely gyueth true peace charyte men fearefully warne ſcolers awaye euery ſo many place ſo many maner wayes worldy kyngdom reherſynge iteratynge ſo ofte kyngdom world ye worlde except man renounce al poſſeſſe item eaſy camell entre nedles iye ryche man entre ī kyngdom heuēs moreouer bothe ſerue god mammon one alſo perable ryche gloton buryed helle ryche man dreamynge enlargynge barnes alſo moſte ſharpe ſore cōmyncacyon thretenyng agaynſt ryche men woo ryche men whiche haue conſolacyon comforte woo whiche full fedde ſhall hungry woo whiche laughe nowe ſhal wayle wepe thyſe ſo many ſayingꝭ chryſte ye ſone god euydent token ynough howe wolde haue dyſcyples ſeruauntes mynded warde thyſe erthely thyngꝭ yet notwithſtandynge benedicte xii whan mylane verona vicentiū mantua rhegiū carariū padway ferrarye mutine argent dyd inſtytute make mayres gouernours ſayd place emperours lodowykes abſence owne vicar deputyes cōmaundynge certayne trybute payde yerely becauſe chryſte kyng heuen therfore pope emperour hedde ruler erthe goodſy reaſon two ſolucyons craftefull apoſtolyke ſpoylynge lodowyke poſſeſſyon italye ſayd power rule empyre owne aſmoche ſoeuer ſucceſſoure peter onely vycar deputie erthe iheſu chryſte kynge heuen praye walke ſpyryte entangle ſelues ſecular worldly buſynes accordynge cōmaundement paule wrytynge thyſe wordes tymothe let man warreth goddes parte entangle hym ſelfe ſeculate buſynes may pleaſe hym c redy hande v two ſolucyons anſweres one byſſhop rome bounden wordes paule moche inferyor perſone hath power auctorytie ouer vpon ſuperyour hym ſelfe alone belongeth bothe ſwerdes whiche ſolucyon thyrde put vnto ſtede auctarye make heaped meaſure thynges ſayd byſſhops becauſe chryſte dyd ſaye thyſe wordes power auctoryte gyuen bothe heuen erthe thyſe wordes haue goten forthe ſelues abſolute perfyte power hereof haue taken ſelfes bothe ſwerdes hereof attrybute ſelues auctoryte aboue councels ye alſo aboue veray goſpels hereof haue chalenged empyre haue caught ſnatched ſelues domynacyon rule neuer haue ende reſte vpon kynges emperours albeit chryſte hath taught v clene contrary thynges men churche ſhuld myniſters lordes wyt ſhulde gather treaſure erthe heuen ſhulde beare croſſe beare threfolde cowne hed golde garnyſſhed precyous ſtones ſhulde mynyſtie ſerue fordes ruler maner faſſhyon lyuynge nowe dayes thus ſcrypture expounded mynde pleaſure thus nowe learne rcceyue take ſenſe meanynge imagyned men ſteade true ſenſe meanynge ſcrypture ſpyryte men ſtede ſpyryte god herken man beleue man obey man chryſtes wordes v nowe doth herken doth beleue yet ſayd ſhepe knoweth voyce agayne parte knowe ſtraunger ronne awaye yf ſhepe chryſte voyce hym onely fleeth ronneth awaye ſtraunger howe praye proue ourſelues ſhepe whiche moſte wretched tyme onely goſpell moreouer hate wolde haue cleane deſtroyed tydde worlde ſayenge churche ſhulde better oh abhomynable impyetye without worde goſpell chryſt whiche euery place teacheth v ſo oft wordes onely cōmaundementes alone obſerued kepte ſayinge hathe cōmaundementes keapeth loneth contrarywyſe thynge dothe ſharply lay iewes charge rebuketh greuouſly yt regarded wordes wold theym whan ſayth yf ſhall abyde wordes ſhal truely dyſcyples ſhall knowe truthe truth ſhall delyuer agayne lytle yt god hereth ye word god therfore becauſe god yf thou ſeche dylygently ranſake holy ſcryture good cryſten reader begynnyng man created thou ſhalt fynde thoſe whiche therin reherſed haue pleaſed god dyd alwayes teache men worde god theyr owne praye dydde euer neither prophetts neyther apoſtels dydde ſpeake teache men thynge worde god moyſes whan heliſeus whan helias ſo forthe ordre vnto laſte prophette ſay maner theſe thynges moyſes ſay theſe thynges helias ſay rather tymes theſe thynges ſayth lorde god whan dyd euer peter whan dyd paule preache theyr owne goſpell el man goſpel iheſu chryſte doth paule playnly openly wytneſſe recorde ye goſpel dyd teache man chryſte boldely curſeth hym euer ye although aungell heuen whiche wolde preſume teache goſpell chryſte beſyde theſe foure golpelles whiche churche dothe onely alowe ezechiell dyd ſe ſpyryte god ſhewyng vnto hym vi c yeres chryſte incarnate expreſſyng perfytefy ye propheſye iiii goſpelles ſymylytude lykenes iiii ſenſyble creature ye whiche fyrſte man ſeconde lyon thyrde oxe fourthe egle eche one whiche iiii lykeneſſes fygured one myſtery chryſt ye lykenes man fygured ye bodely natyuyte hym ſhape lyon ſygnyfyed rorynge great ſounde preachyng goſpell ye myſterye reſurreccyon ye fygure oxe betokened euer laſtyng preſthode ſymylytude egle fygured myſterye dyuynyte godhed vttered ſhewed churche whiche ſhulde ſprede abrode worlde shall churche lacke wante ye goſpels theym holy ghoſte ſelfe gaue euangelyſtes goſpellers owne churche mathew whan publycane called offyce chryſte ſelfe doubte hereof wrote ſette forthe fyrſte goſpell hebrew language iewes whiche conuerted chryſte marcus goſpell goſpel peter ſpecially chryſt dyd ſay fede ſhepe ſo lyke wyſe goſpell whiche luke wrote goſpell paule doctour gentyles whiche attayned vnderſtode ſecreſies pryuyties god whiche lawfull man ſpeke whiche paule prayſe gyuen ſame luke goſpell throughe congregacyons iohn̄ whiche deſerued chryſte hangynge croſſe theſe wordes beholde thy mother contynuall feruent requeſt inſtant deſyre byſſhops aſye theyr ambaſſadours wrote goſpell laſt iiii yet durſte enterpryſe take worke hāde afore ſuche tyme purchaſed mercy fauoure god faſtynge openlye bydden cōmaunded people prayer alſo shall thynke perauenture churche yf pleaſed myght haue forſaken left goſpell whiche wryten obteyned ſo many intreatynges deſyres ſo many ambaſſages moreouer proceſſyons faſtyngꝭ openly cōmaūded wherfore let hym ſoeuer ſcaſely ſeldome obiecte agaynſt v yt theſe goſpelles receyued churche though ben theyr choyſe lybertie alſo haue receyued haue reiected refuſed worde churche ſo auctoryte approue goſpelles lye lykewyſe theyr power dyſalowe ye ſame truthe therfore churche hath approued allowe theſe goſpelles thus moche ſay churche hath gyuen auctoryte theym whiche auctoryte yf pleaſed ye ſame churche myght alſo haue taken worker plato ariſtotyle hathe ben hytherto approued allowed conſent learned men yet man lyghtlye wolde bolde dye truthe ſame workes ſaye churche hathe approued allowed goſpels nothynge el yt churche hathe inſeperablye cleued vndoutable truthe ſayde one fourthe ſygnyfycacyon accepcyon worde certayne cōmune thynge kyndes temperate regymente gouernaunce whether onely one cytie el many cyties whiche ſygnyfycacyon caſſiodorus vſed worde regnum oracyon ſpeche whiche haue made begynnynge boke ſygnyfycacyon alſo woll vſe nowne determynacyons purpoſes nowe owynge deſcrybe tranquyllyte contrarie intranquyllytie lette v ſuppoſe aryſtotell fyrſte fyfte bokes politikes ſeconde thyrde chapytres cytie certayne naturall lyuynge ſenſyble creature lyke cytie cōmuitieis maner beaſte ſenſyble creature whiche well dyſpoſed ordred accordynge nature made certayne proporcionate partes ordred ſette ordre amonge ſelues eche cōmunycatynge theyr workes ſymylytude amonge ſelues alſo hole euen ſo ſame faſcyon cytie cōmunytie made certayne ſuche maner partes yf ſo well ordred inſtytuted accordynge reaſon ſuche maner comparyſon therfore beaſte ſenſyble creature partes vnto hel euen ſuche maner comparyſon ſhall ſeme cōmunytie partes vnto tranquyllytie illacyon true maye take ſure probacyon men comprehende touchynge bothe theym wyt helth tranquyllyte helth al men iugen beſt dyſpoſycyon ſenſyble creature accordynge nature ſo alſo iuge ſaynte helth tranquyllyte tranquyllyte beſte dyſpoſycyon cōmunytie whiche hathe begon inſtytuted accordynge reaſon helthe moſte cūnynge naturall phyloſophers ſaye deſcrybynge good dyſpoſycyon ſenſyble creature whiche euery one partes may perfytely worke operacyons conuenyent agreynge theyr nature accordynge whiche analogye tranquyllyte ſhall good dyſpoſycyon realme cōmunytie whiche euery one membres partes ſayd cōmunytie maye perfytely operacyons conuenyent fytte accordynge reaſon theyr inſtytucyon becauſe whoſoeuer dyffyneth thynges well dothe one tyme gyue knowlege contraryes intranquyllyte ſhal croked euyll dyſpoſycyon ordre realme cōmunytie lykewyſe infyrmyte ſyckenes intranquyllyte diſcorde infirmite ſyckenes croked euyll dyſpoſycion beaſte ſenſyble creature whiche ſome partes letted operacyons workes cōuenyent ſyttynge ſay worke vtterly whytte leſtwyſe letted worke perfytely tranquyllyte therfore contrarye intranquyllyte let thus ſpoken v fyguratly orygynall fyrſte begynnynge cyuyle cōmunytie ¶ thyrde chapytre howe moche haue ſayd trāquyllyte good dyſpoſycyon cōmunytie workynge partes therof conſequētly muſte conſydre cytie cōmunytie ende ordeyned pryncypally whiche howe many pryncypall partes therof moreouer conuenyent operacyon eche one thoſe partes furthermore cauſes ordre ſayd partes amonge ſelues thyſe thynges veray neceſſary profyte determynacyon tranquyllytie contrary intranquyllyte yet al afore treate cytie whiche perfyte cōmunytie dyuerſe kyndes maners therof ought fyrſte brynge declare orygynall begynnynge cyuyle cōmunyties theyr regymentꝭ maners lyuynge whiche beynge leſſe perfyte men dyd procede perfyte cōmunyties regymentes maners lyuynge vſed theym nature alſo arte crafte whiche counterfayteth foloweth nature alwayes sure knowlege thyngeis de whan cauſes knowen procede leſſe perfyte thyngs perfyte men thynke haue ſure knowlege whiche called ſcyence thynge otherwyſe onely whan ſhall haue knowen ye fyrſt cauſes fyrſt pryncyples euen veray orygynall cauſes whiche called elemē ta therfore procedynge accordyng maner ought knowe perceyue cyuyle cōmunyties accordyng dyuerſe regyons ſundry tymes began lytle thynge ſo lytle lytle takynge encreace laſt hathe ben brought cōplement perfeccion lykewyſe haue ſayd yt happeneth cōmeth paſſe euery operacyon worke nature crafte fyrſt whiche fyrſte cō munytie leaſte cōbynacyon cōmunytie humayne cōmunyties whiche cōmunyties ſocyeties hath ſpronge ye copulacyon ſocytie man woman chyef al phyloſophers aryſtotell ſayth fyrſte boke polytykes fyrſte chaptre ſame appereth alſo largyle oeconomykes wherin treateth gouernynge ordrynge howſe howſholde cōbynacyon copulacyon man woman verely men woman brought forth multyplyed whiche fyrſte replenyſſhed onely one howſe mo ſuch maner combynacyons copulacyōs beyng made ſo great ppagacyon increaſe men made one howſe coulde ſuffycyent receyue theym neceſſarye make many howſes pluralytie multytude whiche howſes beynge ioyned togyther called laten tonge vicus vicina englyſſhe ſtrete fyrſt cōmunytie men wryten place afore alleged longe ſtrete men onely one howſe theyr actes dedes namely ſuche actes whiche ſhall hereafter call cyuyle actes ſette ordre hym moſte auncyent moſte aged amonge beynge moſte dyſcrete wyſe yet without lawe cuſtome becauſe lawes cuſtomes coulde yet founde deuyſed onely men yt togyther onely one howſe gouerned maner alſo fyrſt cōmunytie called ſtrete gouerned well nere ſame maner thoughe ſome thynges gouerned ſondry maner albeit gouernoure good man onely one howſe myghte forgyue punyſſhe domeſtycall iniuryes treſpaſſes done within howſe maner wayes euen pleaſure lyſt hym ſelf yet yt lawfull hym ſame preſydent ruler fyrſte cōmunytie called ſtrete cōmunytie neceſſarye whiche moſte auncyent aged ſhuld dyſpoſe ordre ryghtwyſe profytable thynges ſome reaſonable ordynaunce lawe maner naturall becauſe ſemed ſo conuenyent vnto men certayne equyte without great ſerchynge forthe onely ye cōmune iudgemēt reaſon certayne duetye humayne ſocyetie felowſhyp cauſe dyuerſe ſondry maner regymēt gouernaunce one howſe hole ſtrete yf onely one howſe fyrſte oeconomye domeſtycall famylye one brother hadde ſlayne otherwyſe hurte offended brother without daūger ieoperdye therof happenynge folowynge gouenour good man howſe myght lawfully yf wolde haue punyſſhed treſpaſſer extreme ponyſſhement wyt deathe partely becauſe iniurye offence ſemed done onely father whiche dyd forgyue partely becauſe fewneſſe ſmall nombre men tyme alſo becauſe leſſe loſſe heuynes good man howſe lacke one ſone want two whiche thynge alſo fyrſte father adam ſemed whan fyrſte begotten ſone adam punyſſhed chain ſlew brother becauſe pancite ſmalle nōbre men tyme chayn ſlew brother bell properlye cyuyle iuſtyce father ſone wryten v boke etykes treatyſe made ryghwyſnes ye fyrſte cōmunytie called ſtrete neyther lawful neyther lawfull ſo becauſe dyſagrement vnlykenes aforeſayd thynges ye moreouer excepte vengeaunce equalytie iniuryes done ſhuld haue ben made ye moſt ſenyour auncyent myght haue happened nowe myght happen reaſon therof fyghtynge ſeperacyon neyghbours ſtretes multyplyed cōmunytie made larger muſte nedely euer men woman multyplyed propagacyon yet gouerned ſtylle one man defaute lacke many wyſe men elles ſome certayne cauſe wryten thyrde boke polytykes ix cytie men lyuynge cyuyllie onely lyue thyng beaftes alſo bonde men doth alſo lyue wel wyt gyuynge theyr mynde lyberall honeſte workes ben workes vertues practyue alſo ſpeculatyue ſoule ende cyties commune weales good lyfe lyuewel haue thus determyned cytie ordeyned lyuynge well lyuynge fynall ende muſte nowe fyrſte treate lyuynge lyfe maners therof thynge haue ſayde whoſe cauſe cytie inſtytute begon neceſſytie thynges done cōmunytie men ſayd cytie let v therfore groūde vpon vpon pryncyple thynges proued beyng naturally beleued wyllyngly graunted men men hauynge theyr wyttes beynge otherwyſe impedyte letted naturallye al men deſyre hauīge theyr wittes doth deſyre ſuffycyent lyfe moreouer alſo doth refuſe eſchewe noyſome hurtfull thynges thynge alſo onely euydent men alſo al kyndes beaſtes ſenſyble creature accordynge mynde tully fyrſt boke de officiis thyrde chapytre ſayth thus fyrſt euery kynde ſenſyble creature propertye gyuen nature ſaue defende themſelues theyr owne body lyfe eſchewe thoſe thyngꝭ whiche ſemen noyſome hurtfull vnto ſelfe purchaſe gette thoſe thynges whiche neceſſary nedefull preſeruacyon theyr owne lyfe whiche thynge alſo euery man maye perceyue euydently ſenſyble experyence kynde ſenſyble creature lyfe good lyfe conuenyent ſyttyng men two maners one lyfe whiche wordly lyfe heuenly lyfe wonte called temperall wordly lyfe lyfe wont called eternall heuenly lyfe bycauſe hole vnyuerſyte phyloſophers coulde demonſtracyon reaſon proue ſeconde lyfe wytte eternall lyfe neyther thynge euydently knowen hit ſelfe therfore buſyed ſelfes neyther gaue great force eche thyſe thynges whiche neceſſarye gettynge obteynyng ſayd lyfe lyfe lyuynge well good lyfe fyrſt maner temperall wordly thyngꝭ whiche neceſſarye gloryous proude phyloſophers comprehended perceyued demonſtracyon matyer maner complete wherfore obteynynge lyfe cōcluded cyuyle cōmunyte neceſſarye without whiche ſayd cyuyle cōmunytie ſuffycyent lyfe wyſe obtayned amonge whiche phyloſophers pryncypall wytte aryſtoſtle fyrſte boke polytykes ſeconde chapitre ſayd men deſyrous cyuyle cōmunyte naturally haue appetyte vnto herefore whiche thynge albeit ſenſyble experyence doth teache yet notwithſtayndyng woll induce brynge cauſe whiche haue ſayd dyſtynctely ſayenge▪ becauſe man borne naturally made contrarye elementes reaſon cauſe mā ne corrupcyon contrary accyons paſſyons whiche ſayd elementes maner contynually ſomwhat ſubſtaunce corrupted agayne becauſe borne naked vnarmed vndefenced apte ſuffre corrupted deſtroyed exceſſe ayre wherin lyueth elementes hath ben ſhewed naturall phyloſophye nede craftes occupacyons wherfore mā nedeth artes craftes dyuerſe kyndes maners auoyed put aforeſayd incōmodyties annoyaunces whiche artes craftes becauſe maye exercyſed great multytude men neyther may excepte ſayde multytude cōmunycate kepe ſocyetie amōge ſelues one neceſſarye men ſhulde congregate ſelues togyther wynnynge cōmodyouſe profytable auoydynge harme euyll ſayd artes craftes moche amonge men ſo congregated gathered oftentymes chaunceth contencyons bralles ſtryffes whiche excepte ſtrengthened ordred rule iuſtyce myghte cauſe fyghtes bataylles ſeperacyon men ſo concluſyon myght cauſe deſtruccion cytie neceſſarie cōmunycacyon cōmune ſocietie men ordeyne rule iuſtyce one kepe execute ſayd iuſtyce becauſe keper defender executer iuſtyce oughte ponyſſhe iniuryouſe treſpaſſours kepe men beyng within ſame cōmunytie oute cōmunytie whiche eyther trouble ſynguler perſones go aboute oppreſſe cōmunytie neceſſarie cytie ſhuld haue ſomwhat thynge alſo profytable honournnge god neceſſary men ſtate preſent lyfe meane honourynge worſhyppynge god gyuynge thankes vnto hym bothe benefyte receyued hym worlde alſo thoſe receyued worlde come teachynge wherof dyrecte men ſame neceſſarie cytie cyuyle cōmunytie ſhulde determyne aſſygne doctours teach ar neceſſary cyties cyuyle cōmunyties appoynte certayne doctoures teacher theſe thynges party albeit hathe ben ſpoken ſhewed ſomwhat chapytre afore gone yet woll ſpeake ſame agayne dyſtynctely ſuppoſyng fyrſte thynge proued euydently cytie cōmunytie begon ende yt men myght lyue alſo lyue well lyuyng well good lyfe haue determyned cytie cyuyle cōmunytie inſtytute ende mē myghte lyue well afore maye two maner faſcyons one waye maye vnderſtande lyfe wolde wyt temperall wordly lyfe waye maye vnderſtande lyfe worlde come wytte heuenly lyfe whiche two maners lyfe lyuynge whiche deſyred man endes ſhall aſſygne neceſſytie dyſtynecyon partes cyuyle cōmunytie cytie lyfe man lyue fryſt maner wytte wordly temperally otherwhyles taken beynge men lyuynge ſayde ſeconde boke de anima diuere wordly lyfe vuientibus eſt eſſe lyfe lyuynge thynges theyr beynge whiche maner lyfe nothyng elles anima otherwhyles lyfe lyue taken acte accyon paſſion ſoule lyfe agayne thyſe maye taken two maner wayes maye taken vnderſtande vita takē anima eodem eſſe naturali orelles conſimili eſſe whiche call eſſe ſpecificum though lyfe taken eyther thyſe ſayd wayes well lyfe proper man lyfe cōmune hym ſynſyble creaturs doth depende hange naturall cauſes yet preſent conſyderacyon lyfe accyon paſſyon ſoule cōmeth cauſed ſuche maner conſyderacyon made parte naturall phyloſophye whiche treateth de planet et de animalibus preſent inquyſycion conſyderacion tyme take receyue complemente perfeccyon crafte reaſon whiche kynde man lyueth therfore muſte attende note well yf man ought lyue lyue well neceſſarye nedefull accyoris done wel done onely accyons alſo paſſyons ſaye well done ſaye inconuenyent whan man lyueth well temperament becauſe haue receyued nature perfytely euery poynte thoſe thynges whiche thyſe temperament made complete perfyte nedefull man beyonde ouer naturall cauſes reaſon forme faſcyon make ſome thynges whiche operacyon conuerſacyon accyons paſſyons bothe wchynge bodye alſo ſoule myghte made complete profyte thyſe kyndes workes worker procedyng cauſed brought forthe vertues artes ſcyences bothe practyue alſo ſpeculatyue furthermore accyone man two maner accyons paſſyons men alſo paſſyons ſome cōmen brought forthe naturall cauſes without knowledge reaſon vnderſtandynge ben thoſe whiche done cauſed throughe contrarytie elementes wherof bodyes compoſte made reaſon permyxcyon mynglyng theym togyther one kynde accyons operacyons nutrytyue parte power maye conuenyentlye ſayde ſame ſorte alſo accyons elementes cauſe whiche conteyne oure bodyes wherin lyue alteracyon theyr qualyties whiche kynde alſo alteracyons whiche cauſed ye thyngs enterynge mēnes bodyes meates drynkes medycynes poyſons thynges lyke vn theſe accyons paſſyons cauſed v v intellectyue appetatyue power whiche certayne called actiones actiones immanentes immanētes intrinſecall inwarde operacyons becauſe paſſe forthe ſubiecte body doer worker theym neyther exercyſed exteryour organes membres beynge moued wchynge mocyon locall ben thoughtes men alſo theyr deſyres affeccyons called actiones tranſeuntes outwarde actiones trā ſeuntes operacyons becauſe one waye thyſe aforeſayd contrarye theyr maner faſcyon accyons laſte ſpoken wyt inwarde accyons whiche called actiones immanentes temperynge therfore thyſe accyons paſſyons make complete perfyte thynge whiche nature brynge dyuerſe kyndes craftes occupacyons hathe ben founde deuyſed vertues alſo craftes diuyſed haue prophete ezechyel hec ergo lex domus iſte autem menſure altaris therfore ſhall lawe houſe theſe ſhall meaſures altare thyrde ſygnyfycacion worde lex taken tule conteynynge monition imperated volutarye action men ordeyned glorye payne worlde come ſygnyfication lawe moyſes called lawe touchynge ſome parte ſo alſo lawe goſpell touchyng ſelfe hole called lawe wherfore ye apoſtle ſpeakyng theſe two lawes hebrues ſayth thus preeſtode beynge tranſlated neceſſarye muſte nedes trāſlacyon made lawe alſo doctryne ye goſpell called lawe fyrſte chapytre ſaynt iames epyſtle ſaythe thus ſouer ſhall loke perfecte lawe lybertie ſhall contynue c man ſhall blyſſed dede accepcyon ſygnyfycacyon worde ſectes alſo called lawes example ſecte machomete perſians eyther touchynge ſelues hole elles touchynge ſome partes theym albeit amonge theſe onely lawe moyſes lawe goſpel wytte chryſten lawe done conteyne veryte ſygnyfycacion alſo aryſtotle called ſectes lawes ſayde ſeconde phyloſophye howe great lex put ſecte vertue ſtrenght cuſtome lawes done ſhewe agayne xii ſame reliqua veto fabuloſe iam adducta ſunt ad perſuaſionem multorum ad leges et conferens thynges ymagyned brought perſuade many men lawes ſectes theyr profyte fourthly nownelawe moſte famouſly betokeneth knowledge doctryne vnyuerſall iudgement thynges whiche ryghtuous profytable cyuyle cō mynalte contrarye thynges worde lex taken ſygnyfycacyon maye conſydered two maner wayes one waye touchynge lawe maye taken two man̄ wayes owne ſelfe onely ſhewed ryght wronge profytable noyſome hurtefull thus ſcyence doctryne ryght called lawe maner waye maye conſydered precepte gyuen obſeruacyon fulfyllynge ſayde lawe vnder payne rewarde dyſtrybuted fulfyller breaker preſent worlde elles gyuen maner ſuche precepte cōmaū dement worde conſydered maner moſte properly ſygnyfycacyons called lawe worde taken ſygnyfycacyon aryſtotle dothe defyne x boke ethikes ix chapytre ſaythe thus lawe hathe power compell whiche ſpeache made ſome wyſdom reaſon wytte polytyke reaſon whiche ordre dyſpoſe ryghtuous profytable thynges contrary thyn ge lawe hathe coactyue power moche precepte cō maumedement gyuen lawe ſhulde obſerued whiche precepte men howe ye lawes acoactiue precept compelled kepe obſerue el becauſe lawe gyuen maner ſuche precepte wherfore true cognycyons knowledge thynges ryghtuouſe profytable cyuyle cōmynalte lawes oneles ſuche coactyue precepte commaundemente gyuen obſeruacyon theym elles ſo haue ben gyuen maner precepte albeit ſuche true knowledge ſayde thynges neceſſaryly requyred perfyte lawe yea moreouer otherwhyles falſs knowledgs iudgemēts rightwyſe profytable thing ar made lawes cōmaundement gyuen ſhulde obſerued el yf gyuen maner precept appereth regyons certayne barbarous people whiche cauſe obſerued ryghtuouſe thyng murtherer manqueller ſhal quyet abſolued cyuyle blame cyuyle payne punyſſhement ſo paye money ſome thynge value ſuch maner offence yet thynge playne vtterly ryght ſo conſequently lawes theym vtterly vnperfecte caſe put graunted ſayd lawes haue due forme wytte coactyue precepte theyr obſeruacyon yet wante lacke due condycyon wyt due trueordynacyon ryghtfull ryght vnder accepcyon ſygnyfycacyon worde lex comprehended rule cyuyle ryghtes vtylyties whiche rule haue ben inſtytuted y• auctoryte man cuſtomes ſtatutes ordenaunces actes made cōmens decretalles lyke rule whiche haue ſayd grounded vpon auctoryte man yet ought knowe aſ well lawe goſpell lawe moyſes peraduenture ſectes dyuerſely conſydered compared hole parte theym vnto actes men ſtate preſent worlde worlde come otherwhyles dothe belonge hathe belonged hytherto ſhall belonge thyrde ſygnyfycacyon worde lex otherwhyles laſte ſygnyfycacyon ſayd worlde ſhall opened declared largely viii ix ſeconde diccion certeyne yt ſayd lawes ſectes touchynge accordynge trouthe certayne theym touchynge falſe imagynacyon fantaſye vayne promyſe thus certayne rule lawe cyuyle actes men appereth euydently theſe thynges whiche haue ſayde ¶ neceſſyte makynge lawes takynge worde moſte proper ſygnyfycacyon expedyent prynce gouernour neuer ſo moche vertuous ryghtu ous gouerne without lawes xi chapytre howe haue thus dyuyded worde lawe accepcions ſygnyfycacions wyll ſhewe fynall cauſe wher neceſſytie makynge lawes declared fore neceſſarye lawes haddetakynge worde laſte moſte propre ſygnyfycacyon moſte pryucypall cauſe cyuyle ryghte cōmen vtylyte profyte nexte cauſe certayne ſecuryte prynces gouernoures ſpecyally namely thoſe whiche gouernoures inherytaunce ſucceſſyon blode alſo diuturnite longe contynuaunce theyr gouernaunce power auctoryte neceſſarye haue lawes former cauſe wytte cyuyle ryght cōmen profyte proue thus neceſſary ordeyne thynge cōmen weale cyuyle cōmynalte without whiche cyuyle iudgementes wyſe well gyuen whiche gyuen duelye ſo ought whiche alſo preſerued defalte moche poſſyple actes men ſuche maner thynge lawe gouernour appoynted gyue cyuyle iudgementes accordynge ergo inſtytucyon makynge lawe neceſſarye cōmen welthe fyrſte propoſicion ſyllogiſme maner euydent knowen ſelfe nere vnto fyrſte pryncyples called whiche proued thynge euydent ſelues certentie wherof alſo ought maye taken v chapitre diccion vii parte therof ſeconde propoſycion demonſtracyon ſhall made euydent ſayeng completemēt iudgement goodnes ſaye iudgement perfectely good requyred ryght vncorrupte affeccyon iudges alſo true knowledge thyngꝭ iudged contrary whiche two thynges done corrupte cyuyle iudgementꝭ croked wronge lewde affeccyon iudgꝭ corrupted throughe euyll affeccyon iudge hatted loue couetouſnes puerteth ye deſyre iudge al theſe thyngꝭ kept away iudgement iudgment preſerued theſe iudge gouernour ſhal appoynted aſſygned gyue iugementꝭ accordynge lawes becauſe lawe without peruerſe affeccyon made onely frende enemye hym dothe good hym y• doth hurte made vnyuerſally generally hym ſoeuer yt doth cyuylye wel cyuylye euyll thyngꝭ ar accidentall lawe without lawe ſo without iudge perſones whiche ſette iudged maye eyther frendes enemyes profytable noyſome perſones hym ſytteth iudge gyuynge promyſynge ſomwhat eyther good euyll hym ſo lykewyſe ſuche intencyons whiche maye cauſe iudge affeccyon peruertynge corruptynge iudgement whiche conſyderacyon maner iudgement moche poſſyble oughte cōmytted put togyther arbytrement wyll pleaſure derye fewe thynges cōmyted pleaſur iudges iudge oughte determyned lawe ſentence iudgement pronounced gyuen accordynge ſame lawe ſentence aryſtotle thyrde polytykes xi chapytre wherin purpoſynge ſerche wherther better cōmen wele gouerned beſte man without lawe elles beſte lawe ſaythe wyſe thyng better gouerne iudge whiche hathe paſſyon ſaye maner affeccyon whiche maye peruerte iudgement thyng whiche hath paſſyons hit ſelfe nature lawe without ſuche maner paſſyon affeccyon mynde euery man muſte nedes haue paſſyons ſayth euery man exceptyng man mānes mynde without ſynyſter affeccyons neuer ſo vertuous whiche ſentence repetynge agayne fyrſte boke rhetorikes fyrſte chapytre ſayth thus omnium quidem maximū quer • tur ſcilicet nihil aſ que lege iudicandum relinque debet arbitrio iudicātis c ſay thynges moſte neceſſarye thynge lefte arbytryment pleaſure iudge iudged without lawe quia iudicium legiſlatoris thynge iudged without lawe c iudgement lawe maker ſaye lawe made pertyculer perſon thynges come generall thynges offycer iudge ſyttynge iudgement iudge thyngꝭ preſent determynate ꝑtyculer thyngꝭ theſe wyt gouernour iugde oftentymes annexed loue hatred deſyre theyr owne ſynguler profyte ſo yet ſuffycyently ſe trouthe ryghte iudgement dothe regarde hathe reſpecte iudgemente theyr owne propre pleaſure profyte elles theyr owne dyſpleaſure dyſprofyte alſo ſayth ſame fyrſte boke ſeconde chapytre ſayth thus gyue lyke maner iugementes glad mery iugementes geuen aft er dyuers maners whan ſad ſorye whan loue whan hate agayne iugemente corrupted otherwhyles reaſon ignoraunce iudges thoughe good affeccyon intencyon whiche euyll defaute taken awaye ſupplyed lawe becauſe determyned maner parfyghtly ryght wronge profytable noyſome hurtfull touchynge euery one cyuyle actes men thynge coulde ſuffycyently done one man alone yet peraduēture men one tyme coulde able fynde deuyſe kepe holde rememberaunce cyuyle actes whiche determyned lawe ye moreouer euer fyrſte fynders deuyſers lawe whiche begynnynge vnperfyte finyſſhed made perfyte addicyons yt come alſo men ſame tyme whiche obſeruyd marked cyuyle actes men dyd ſaye ſmall thynge vnperfyghte whiche afterwarde made perfyghte fynyſſhed addycyons thoſe men came theyr tyme thynge eaſye ynoughe perceyue experience haue ſome thynges haue ben added lawes ſome thynges taken awaye ſame whyles howe lawes hathe ben chaunged cōtrary accordynge dyuerſyte age alſo accordynge dyuerſyte ſtate tymes euen one ſame age hereunto aryſtotle beareth wytneſſe ſeconde boke polytykes thyrde chapytre whan ſayd thus thynge ought knowe ought haue reſpecte loke vnto longe tyme many yeres long delyberacyon taken ſentence lawe pronounced aforegone whiche yeres muſte knowe whether theſe thynges haue done well el wyt theſe thynges whiche ought inſtytuted ordayned lawes ſame ſayth alſo fyrſt boke thetorykes fyrſt chapytre afterwardes ſayth geuynge lawes made thynges hath ben conſydered delyberacyon long ſeaſon thynge confyrmed reaſon makynge gyuynge lawes requyreth nedeth prudence wyſdome appered heretofore deſcrypcion worde lawe wyſdome requyreth longe experyence experyence requyreth prudence requyreth long experyence longe tyme wherfore vi boke ethikes viii chapytre wryten thus token whiche haue ſayde many yonge men geomatricions mathematycans wyſe hauynge knowlege ſuche thynges therfore euen prudent cauſe hereof becauſe prudence ſynguler pertyculer thynges whiche made knowen experyence nowe yonge man wanteth experyence longe maketh experte man contynuaunce tyme cauſeth maketh experyence therfore whiche one man alone fyndeth may knowe hym ſelfe alone well knowlege thynges ryghtuous profytable cyuyle cōmunyte ſciences lytell el thynge agayne alſo artes ar made perfyte one man alone men one age tyme obſerue marke vnperfyghte thynge comparyſon thynge whiche obſerued marked men many dyuers age tymes therfore ariſtotle treatynge theinuencyon fyndynge trouth touchynge euery arte dyſcyplyne ſcyence ſecōde boke phyloſophie fyrſt chapitre ſayth thus concernyng inuencyon arte ſcyence deuyſed one man wyt onely lytle thynge aſſured truthe ſame ſcyence founde hym yt gathered togyther ſame ſcyence wittes many men may drawe ſome quantytie truthe tranſlacyon arabical tonge texte open playne meanynge wherof eche one wyt deuyſers fynders maner arte dyſcyplyne perceyued outher lytell el nothynge verytie trouthe whan thoſe thynges ſhal gathered togyther whiche al men hath comprehē ded obſerued marked hoole ſhal amounte ſūme quantite greatnes whiche thynge maye moſte euydentlie perceyuyd ſcyence aſtronomye ſo helpe men haue amonge ſelues eche one addycyon thynges afterwardes founde vnto thyngs wher craftes hathe takē theyr perfeccyon afore founde craftes dyſcyplynes hathe receyued pefeccyon whiche thynge aryſtotle fygurallie example declareth ſame place aboute inuēcyon fyndynge muſyke whan ſayd yf timotheus ben ſhuld haue moche melodie ſhuld lacke great parte muſyke yf phrynes ben tymothe ſhuld neuer haue ben ſo perfyghte melodyes fyrſte inuentours muſyke wyt yf thynges inuented afore phrines whiche wordes auerois expoundynge ſeconde cōmente ſayth thus whiche aryſtotle ſaythe chapitre euydent manyfeſte man may able hym ſelfe inuente fynde practyue ſpeculatyue ſcyences parte made complete perfyghte helpe beforehath lefte hym foloweth cōmeth ſame ſayth laſt chapytre ſeconde boke eleuches inuencyon retoryke ſcyences howe ſoeuer inuencyon logyke whiche ariſtotle aſcribeth perfyghtlie holye hym aryſtotle boſteth hym ſelf alone haue ben fyrſte inuenter logyke ſelfe alone without ye inuēcyon helpe man yt afore tyme wherin ſemeth haue ben ſyngulare amonge ſaythe viii boke etikes fyrſt chapitre two men ioynynge ſelues togyther may able perceyue vnderſtāde thou one man alone yf ſo two men may perceyue moch moo two togyther alſo ſucceſſyuelie may perceyue one man alone whiche ariſtotle ſaythe concernynge preſent purpoſe thyrde politikes xi chapitre perauenture ſhall ſeme ſome man agaynſt reaſon one man ſhulde perceyue dyſcerne better iudgynge ii iyes ii eares el ſhulde worke better ii feete ii handes many men many iyes eares feete hādes moche therfore lawe iye made many iyes ſaye comprehencyon knowlege examyned many comprehenſyons lawe ſignyfyed olde wyſe men iye auoydynge erroure aboute cyuyle iudgmentes iudgynge ryght well ſure waye leſſe ieopardouſe ſuch iudgementes done accordynge lawe accordynge arbrytrement wyll pleaſure iudge cauſe neceſſarie lawe made ſet yf cōmune weales ſhulde well ordred touchynge cyuyle ryghtes vtylytyes lawe cyuyle iudgementes preſerued ignoraunce peruerſe croked affeccyon whiche elles myght iudges ſeconde propoſycyon minor call demonſtratiue ſillogiſme whiche begynnynge wherfore lawes neceſſarie chapytre haue gone boute proue neceſſarie lawes cōmune weale howe maner ſtryfe cyuyle cauſe controuerſie ryſen whiche determyned lawe ought defyned determyned iudged ſhall ſhewed xiiii chapitre let iudge determine nothynge without lawe diccyon conclude lawes neceſſarie excludynge malyce erroure ignoraunce iudges cyuyle iudgementes ſentences theſe conſyderacyons aryſtotle counſayled iudge gouernour ſhuld graunted arbrytrement fre lybertie iudge cōmaunde cyuyle mater without lawe ſuche thynges wherin law myght haue determyned wherfore v boke etikes ſyxte chapytre aryſtotle treatynge iuſtyce iniurye ſaythe wyſe cauſe ſuffre man gouerne rule acordyng reaſon wyt accordynge lawe aſſygneth cauſe afore alledged wyt peruerſe croked affeccyon whiche maye happen chaunce hym alſo thyrde boke politikes vii chapytre ſaythe thus anſwere fyrſte doubte queſtyon euydent open none thynge ought ſo moche gouerne rule lawes whiche well made ſay whiche gouerneth ruleth accordynge lawes ſame alſo ſayth ſame iii boke xii chapytre wyſe ſoeuer therfore byddeth wylleth lawe gouerne rule ſemeth byd wyll god lawes gouerne byddeth wylleth man gouerne vnderſtande without lawe owne pleaſure ioyneth putteth alſo beeſte ſheweth cauſe ſo ſayth lytle ſayenge propter quod ſine appetitu intellectus lex eſt ſhulde ſaye goodly ſentence lawe vnderſtandynge knowledge reaſon without appetite luſte ſaye without affeccyon ſame ſentence repeteth alſo fyrſt boke retorykes fyrſt chapytre ſaythe thus moſt conuenyent therfore well made lawes determyne thynges ſoeuer doth happen chaunce cōmytte fewe thynges arbrytrement ye iudges aſſygneth afore alledged cauſes wyt excluſyon auoydynge malyce ignoraunce iudges cyuyle iudgementes ſayd malyce erroure ignoraunce chaū ce lawe lykewyſe maye iudges hathe ben ſhewed aryſtotle ſpeaketh largelye thus openlye iiii boke politikes iiii chapytre ſayenge wyſe lawes gouerne rule ſaye prynces ruler gouerne accordynge lawes cōmune weale vnderſtande thou temperate well ordred lawe ought gouernoure ruler ouer nowe reſteth remayneth ſhewe prynces gouernoures ought gouerne accordynge lawe without beſyde namelye moſte theſe prynces kynges whiche made gouernours al theyr yſſue ofſprynge theyr kyngdome powre maye ſure maner ieopardye peryll alſo may endure cōtynue longer whiche ſecondarie fynall cauſe neceſſyre lawes aſſygned hus begynnynge chapitre fyrſte may proued becauſe gouerne rule accordynge lawes preſerueth iudgmentes ſayde gouernoures defaulte whiche myght happen reaſon ignoraunce peruerſe affeccyon whiche lawes beynge guyded well ordred theyr owne ſelues towarde theyr cōmunes ſubiectes leſſe ſuffre ſedycyons ſo conſequentlye leſſe ſuffre ſolucyons deſtruccyons theyr kyngdomes whiche myght happen chaunce doynge lewdlie accordynge theyr wyll pleaſure aryſtotle ſayth openlye v boke polytykes x chapytre regnum ſayth ſaye kyngdome ſeldome lytle deſtroyed thoſe thynges whiche extrynſecall without ſelfe ſelfe intrynſecall cauſes chaunceth thynge deſtroyeth kyngdomes ofte corrupted deſtroyed ii maner wayes one whan ſedicyon ryſeth betwene partyners kyngdome ſeconde waye whan begyn rule gouerne tyrannouſly deſyrynge wyffynge fordes many contrarye lawe perauenture ſome man wyll obiecte agaynſt ſaye beſt man good man without ignoraunce peruerſe croked affeccyon let hus make anſwere ſaye cōmeth paſſe ſeldome thoughe chaunce one good man without paſſyons yet ſo moche without ye lawes haue ſhewed heretofore auctoryte aryſtotle reaſon ſenſyble experyence euery mānes ſoule mynde hath whyles ſome ſynyſtre affeccyon whiche thynge maye byleue yt whiche red iiii chapytre danyel mēcyon made yt came ii preeſtes wycked mynde purpoſe agaynſt suſāna yt myght put deth hyſtorye suſanne olde men preeſtes iudges people yt yere al notwithſtādynge yet gaue falſe teſtymony wytneſſe agaynſt becauſe ſhe wold cōſent applye ſelfe theyr wycked fylthie cōcupyſcēce luſt nowe therfore yf preeſtes aged men man wolde lytle thynke corrupted throughe catnall concupyſcence howe moche couetouſnes vyces thought men doubtles man▪ neuer ſo vertuous without peruerſe corrupte affeccyon ignoraunce ſo lawe therfore moſt ſure way cyuyle iudgementes dyrected lawe cōmytted arbytrement wyll iudge neuer ſo vertuouſe man caſe put admytted whiche ſeldome thynge maner impoſſyble prynce gouernoure ſo heroycall paſſynge vertuous coulde neyther paſſyon neyther ignoraunce hym yet may ſones ſhall ſubiecte ſome ſynyſtre euyll affeccyon wherof rulynge accordynge theyr wylfull affeccyon without certayne lawe ordre may enſue moche inconuenyence whiche yf ye wyll replye ſaynge yt theyr father beynge ſo good man ſuppoſed peraduenture wyl delyuer powre auctoryte anſwere ſuche ſayenge beleaued regarded partlye becauſe lyeth hym depryue ſucceſſyon inherytaunce kyngdome moche due belongeth ſucceſſours yſſue kynred partelye becauſe althoughe powre tranſlate regall powre vnto ſoeuer lyſt yet wolde dyſheryte owne ſones neuer ſo lewde vngracyous thynge wherof cōmenlye hathe knowledge wherfore aryſtotle thyrde boke politikes xi chapytre anſwerynge obieccyon ſayth wyſe eaſye beleue wyt father wyll dyſheryte owne ſones kyngdome powre harde thynge greatter vertue belongeth nature man wherfore expedyent prynces gouernours rather ruled determyned lawe gyue cyuyle iudgementes theyr owne wyll pleaſure doynge accordynge y• lawe ſhal nothyng ſhal otherwyſe well worthy reproue reaſon wherof theyr kyngdome powre ſhall made ſure daunger alſo contynuall durable cauſe counſayle moſt excellent phyloſopher aryſtotle vnto prynces gouernours wherof take lytell heade fyfthe boke ye politikes xi chapytre whan ſayde thus fewer thyngꝭ haue powre ouer vnderſtāde thou without lawe ſo moche longer tyme euery kyngdome powre muſte nedes contynue wyt prynces gouernours ſelues leſſe lordely made demure theyr maners alſo leſſe enuyed theyr ſubiectes bryngeth teſtymonye certayne wyſe kynge gouernoure called theopompus whiche gaue hym parte theopōpue powre auctoryte graunted vnto hym wherfore haue iudged conuenyent brynge texte wordes aryſtotle becauſe ſyngularyte excellent vertue prynce ſuche neuer maner hath ben herde ſpace many hendreth yeres haue ben prynce wordes aryſtotle theſe afterwardes theopōpus meaſur •• ge example theopompus ſaye mynyſſhynge bryngynge meane powre whiche peraduenture ſemyd excede meaſure added offyce auctoryte whiche called ephory dede mynyſſhynge powre wytte owne powre yet makynge regall powre increaſynge tyme ſaye makynge durable wherfore certayne maner made leſſe ſo men ſaye anſwered wyfe whan ſhe aſked queſtyon hym whether aſhamed leaue regall powre leſſe ſones father lefte hym verely ſaythe leaue nowe moch durable heroycallvoyce theopompus procedynge metuaylous great wyſdome greatly noted whiche without lawes wyll vſe fulnes powre ouer theyr ſubiectes whiche ſentence many prynces gouernoures nothynge markynge takynge hede haue fall haue ben deſtroyed ſelues haue ſene lawefull prynce greue ſubiectes eyaccyon contrary beſyde without lawe nowe tyme lacke takynge hede hereof leaſte kyngdome maner hole lyke deſtroyed whyles certayne prynce gouernoure therof wolde haue charged ſubiectes layde vpon theyr neckes certayne vnwonte exaccyon contrarye lawe theſe thynges whiche haue ſayd euydent open lawes neceſſarye cōmune weales yf ought vtterly well ordered kyngdomes regall power cōtynue longe endure ¶ effectyue cauſe lawes man cauſe whiche maye proued demonſtratyue ſillogyſme alſo cauſe whiche proued demonſtracyon whiche thyng nought elles ſerche lawe maker xii chapytre howe foloweth conſequentlye ſpeke effectyue cauſe lawes whiche cauſe may ſhewed demonſtracyon inſtytucyon lawes whiche poſſyble made hathe ben made imedyatly worke reuelacyon oracle god without mannes arbytrement wyll whiche maner ſayde fore lawe moyſes haue ben inſtytuted euen alſo touchynge thoſe preceptes cyuyſe actes whiche ſtate preſente worlde entende make aſſygnacyon onely inſtytucyon lawes prynces gouernours made brought forthe cauſed īmedyatly wyll arbytrement mynde man vnto whiche aſſygnacyon begynnynge entre let hus ſaye fynde lawe taken materyallie accordynge thyrde ſygnyfycacyon wytte knowledge thynges ryghtuouſe thynges profytable cōmune weale cyuyle cōmunyte may belonge appertayne dyſcrypcyon lawe maner cytezen perſone cyuyle cōmunyte albeit inquyſycyon maye conuenyentlie done obſcruacyon may intende ſuche inquyſycyon moſte aged men hauynge moſte experyence cyuyle actes whome call predent worldlye wyſe men conſyderacyon artyfycers handycraftes men whiche muſt intende dylygently applye ſelues theyr workes occupacyons gette thynges neceſſarye ſuſtentacyon theyr lyfe becauſe true knowledge inuencyon thynges ryghtuouſe thynges profytable cyuyle cōmunyte theyr contraryes lawe accordynge laſt moſte propre ſygnyfycacyon worde whiche made meaſure cyuyle actes men vnleſſe whan coactyue precepte ſhall haue ben gyuen obſeruacyon therof elles hathe ben gyuen maner ſuche precepte hym whoſe auctoryte trangreſſoures ought maye ponyſſhed therfore conuenyent accordynge tell ſhewe perſone perſones auctoryte belongeth gyuynge ſuche
