ſayenge vnderſtanded non crederem euāgelio niſi catholice eccleſie aucthoritas cōmoueret auctoryte churche dyd moue maye accordynge thynges aforeſayd vnderſtanded two maner wayes haue two ſences one beleued ſcrypture goſpell ſaye ioyfull meſſage chryſte teſtymonye churche albeit yt dyd beleue ſcrypture goſpell contayne truthe pryncypally peraduenture ſome myracle ſome reuelacion elles faythe whiche dyd beleue yt chryſte god ſo conſequentlye al tradycion doctryne trewe obſerued kepte ſence whiche ſayde wordes auguſtyne may haue dyd fyrſte begynnynge receyue beleue bothe theſe aforeſayde thynges teſtymonye churche albeit fyrſte ſence theſe two ſemeth agree vnto ſayenge apoſtle fyrſt chapytre galathians wordes ſayenges chryſte god ar therfore trewe becauſe churche doth ſo wytneſſe true teſtymonye therfore wytnes teſtymonye churche true ye iudgement churche trewe ſhe alledgeth true ſayenge chryſte whiche make ſayengꝭ true becauſe true wherfore apoſtle galathiās afore alledged ſayth thus thoughe aūgel heuen preache vnto thynge otherwyſe haue preached vnto curſed lykewyſe vnderſtanded althoughe holy churche preached goſpell ſay contrary goſpell ſhulde haue ben true cauſe paule thus ſayd ſure doubte ſayde goſpell ſayenge reuelacyon chryſte whiche coulde falſytie therfore ſoeuer ſence aforeſayd wordes ſaynt auguſtyne expounded ar contrarye agaynſt ſentēce haue ſayd ſaynt auguſtyne dothe ſo moche ſaye beleueth goſpell auctoryte churche becauſe toke begynnynge beleue churche fayth otherwhyles begynneth hearynge agayne becauſe moued good lyuynge holy conuerſacyon churche pacyent ſufferaunce trybulacyon whiche perceyued churche tyme perſecucyon ¶ xx xxi xxii chapytres lefte moche value auoyde offence ſome ſpyrytuall perſons beare peper theyr noſes yt iudge euery truth ſpoken malyce ¶ dyuerſe maners ſygnyfycaciōs fulnes powre maye taken maner ordre byſſhop rome hath taken theſe vnto hym breyfly generallye maner faſcyon hathe vſed dothe vſe xxiij chapytre fulnes powre maye one waye truely vnderſtanded howe many maner wayes fulnes powre maye taken taken powre whiche able maner acte poſſyble vpon maner thynge voluntarylye powre ſaye hauynge exceſſe whiche maner powre ſemeth agreynge belōgynge onely vnto chryſte wherfore ſayde laſte mathewe al powre gyuen bothe heuen erthe ¶ ſeconde waye fulnes powre may vnderſtanded purpoſe powre whiche maye lawfull man exercyſe maner acte maner man maner outwarde thynge beynge powre men ordynable vſe men elles agayne powre accordynge whiche man maye exercyſe maner acte albeit vpon euery maner man vpon maner thynge beynge ſubiecte powre man elles agayne powre accordynge vnto whiche may laufull exercyſe maner actes onely acte operacyon determyned kynde maner yet accordynge maner inclynacyon appetyte wyller vpon maner man euery thynge beynge ſubiecte vnder powre man ¶ iiii way fulnes powre may vnderſtanded laſt aforeſayd powre powre accordynge maner aforeſayde vpon clarkes onely powre inſtytutynge eccleſiaſticall offyces depryuynge depoſynge ſayd offyces dyſtrybutynge eccleſiaſticall temporalles benefyces accordynge maner laſte afore reherſed ¶ v waye fulnes powre may vnderſtanded powre whiche belongeth preeſtes maner wayes bynde loſe men ſynnes paynes done excōmunycate interdycte reconcyle whiche powre haue ſpoken ¶ vi waye fulnes powre maye vnderſtanded powre whiche maye laufull put handes vpon men receyuynge eccleſiaſticall ordres gyue prohybyte holde ſacramentes churche whiche powre hath ben ſpoken ¶ vii waye fulnes powre maye vnderſtanded powre interpretynge ſcrypture ¶ viii laſt way touchynge purpoſe fulnes powre maye vnderſtanded powre paſtorall cure ſoules generall comparyſon people prouynces world hath ben ſpoken agayne fulnes powre maye vnderſtanded accordynge eche one aforeſayd dyuyſyons powre determyned lawe powre may vnderſtanded full powre determyned lawes man god vnder whiche ryght reaſon may cō uenyently comprehended peraduenture certayne maners combinacions fulnes powre thynke haue reherſed rekened vp whiche appertayneth purpoſe intended v ¶ theſe dyuyſyons fulnes powre thus premyſed declared ſaye fulnes powre accordynge two fyrſte maners ſygnyfycacyons aforeſayd doth wyſe agre appertayne byſſhop rome byſſhop preeſt ſaue onely chryſt god two paſſe ouer becauſe thynge euydent becauſe hath ben certyfyed wyſdome god man morall ſcyence alſo becauſe ſpede breyfnes touchynge thyrde iiii way maner fulnes powre hathe ben proued demonſtracyon ſtronge reaſon xv chapytre fyrſte dyccyon moreouer cōfyrmed holy ſcrypture ye iiii v viii dyccion agayne moſte ſtablyſſhed coroberated xv xvi xvii xxi dyccyon ſuche maner powre onely fulnes alſo dothe lawe god agree appertayne preeſte byſſhop yt ſuche one vpon man beynge clarke clarke concernynge two wyt ye v vi maners fulnes powre hathe ben ſhewed vi vii chapytours dyccion powre byndynge louſynge ſynnes paynes dewe lyke wyſe powre curſynge excōmunycatynge man openlye graū ted preeſte abſolutelye fulnes determyned law god ſo neyther cōdempne thoſe innocentes afore god neyther louſe gyltye afore god moreouer ſame powre inſtytute eccleſiaſticall mynyſters puttynge handes teache preache mynyſtre ſacramentes churche cōmunyties chryſten men dothe ſo fully agree belonge byſſhoppes preeſtes determyned appoynted vnto lawe god man conuenyent maner workynge accordynge touchynge two maners fulnes powre remaynynge wyt vii viii hathe ben ſhewed agree appertayne preeſte byſſhop fulnes accordynge determynacyon bothe lawe god lawe man ¶ therfore conclude fulnes powre doth agree appertayne neyther byſſhop rome neyther byſſhop preeſte ſuch one ¶ nowe conſequentlye ſhewed whenſe whiche ſygnyfycacion byſſhop rome toke fyrſt begynnynge aſcribynge tytle fulnes powre vnto hym ſelfe albeit dede doth agree belonge vnto hym foreſayd ſygnyfycacions appereth byſſhop rome toke fyrſt tytle fulnes powre vnto hym ſelfe viii ſygnyfycacion begynnynge apparente appertaynynge therof vnto hym ſayenge chryſte whiche xxi iohn̄ ſpeakynge vnto ſaynt peter ſaythe fede ſhepe agayne becauſe ſayd ſyngulerly ſame peter xvi mathewe ſhall gyue keyes kyngdom heuens c agayne ſayd peter xviii iohn̄ turne thy ſworde thy ſcaberde moreouer ye anſwere whiche dyſcyples made chryſte ſayenge se two ſwerdes textes theyr owne interpretacyons certayne men wyll vnderſtā ded vnyuerſyte hole flocke ſhepe al worlde wyt chryſten men cōmytted peter onely ſo lykewyſe euery biſſhop rome ſpecyall vycar ſaynt peter apoſtles byſſhops ſucceſſours vnyuerſyte whole flocke ſhepe whole worlde eche one one determynate pertyculare flocke prouynce hath ben cōmytted gouerned ¶ byſſhop rome taken vnto hym ſelfe tytle fulnes powre albeit accordynge trewe ſence ſcrypture ſhall ſuffycyentlye ſhewed xxviii chapytre dyccyon preſumpcion went ſygnyfycacyon peraduenture becauſe lucre auauntage elles vſurpe ſome cōmodyte profyte excellencie aboute men wyt takynge vpon hym ſelfe preachynge openly alone ſeuerallye maye maner ſoeuer ſhall pleaſe hym worde vtterlye exempte delyuer aſſoyle ſynners paynes purgatorye ſo calleth ¶ theſe ſygnyfycacions ſo taken vnder certayne coloure appetaunce pytie mercye ende fyrſte myght ſeme charyte take thought care men ſecondaryly myght ſuppoſed haue powre wyllynge haue mercy pytie vpon al men byſſhops rome beynge ſtrēgthed pryuyleges grauntes emperours lowedely lye cheyfly emperyal ſeate beynge vacante dyd extende ſtretche forth tytle fyrſt ordeynynge makynge certayne lawes vpon clarkes preeſtes concernynge eccleſiaſticall cuſtomes ceremonyes whiche begynnynge called decree afterwardes howe wherfore faſtynges certayne kyndes meates certayne dayes cam fyrſte vp fyrſt receyued waye maner requeſtes exhortacyons perſwaded certayne ordynacyons laye men faſtes abſtynence certayne meatꝭ certayne tymes ye obtaynīge ye helpe mercy god take away certayne peſtylēcꝭ infeſciones ayre men raygned yt tyme appereth euydently legende ſaynt gregory certayne ſayntes laye men theyr owne free wyll taken receyued ſuche abſtynences becauſe deuocyon longe cuſtome obſerued ſuche free ordynaunces whiche ſayd haue ben requeſtes exhortacyons tyrantes rome began cōmaunde openly ſame thyngꝭ maner precepte law ſo bolde without ye lycēce colour religyon hath ſprō ge moch myſchefe worldly prynces ſtryke trangreſſoures therof terroure drede theyr curſe excōmunycacyon yet vnder coloure apperaunce relygyon honorynge god afterwardes theyr appetytes hauynge mynyon increaſynge whan perceyued alſo deuout chryſten men greatly put feare ſuche maner wordes throughe ignoraunce foloweth folyſſhe feare fonde obieccyons wyſe men day ben nowe fearefulnes ignoraunce lawe god whiche beleued ſelues bounde vnto thoſe thynges whiche cōmaunded preeſtes feare eternall dethe byſſhoppes rome theyr companye clarkes preſumed ſtatute make certayne oblygarchicall decree ordinacyons concernynge cyuyle actes whiche pronounced ſelues euery one dyd take theyr ordre offyce clarkeſhyp vpon yea beynge pure laye men exempted publyke cōmune charge promotynge vnto offyce euyn ſeculare men maryed whiche ſoone allured therunto myght enioye īmunite fredom cōmune publyke charge reaſon wherof made lytle parte cyuyle multytude ſubiectꝭ vnto ſelues withdrawynge powre gouernaūce ſeculare prynces gouernours agayne purpoſynge goynge aboute exempcion clarkes withdrawe greatter multytude pronounced decree yt thoſe ſtryken payne curſynge ſoeuer ſhall haue done perſonall iniuryes deuyll latten loſe blowe trompettes ſoeuer vnto haue ben taken vnto companye clarkes defamynge alſo openlye church thoſe dothe iniurye clarkes excōmunycacyon leſſe perſuynge ſame men therfore requyre haue punyſſhed penaltes curſynges money temporall lawes foloweth deteſtable thynge verye execrable offyce preeſtes byſſhoppes rome certayne byſſhoppes intent maye ampliate enlarge theyr owne iuryſdyccyon theyr moſte fylthy lucre vnto contempt god manyfeſt preiudyce ſeculare prynces dothe excōmunycate ſhyt ſacramentes churche well laye men clarkes beynge peraduenture lytle neglygent regardynge elles beynge vtterly vnable paye certayne dettes money payment wherof formally bounde vntyll certayne terme tyme appoynted whiche laye men clarkes chryſte mayne exhortacyons paynes labour laſte owne marterdome precyous blode hathe put ſet within churche dyd paule whiche made facyons vnto men intente paule myght wyn men chryſte wolde ſynners ſhulde cut away company chryſten men onely great greuouſe offē ce hathe ben ſhewed v fyrſte epyſtle corinthyans yet beynge contente herewith deſyrynge domynyon hygheſt gouernaunce ſeculare men contrarye precepte chryſte apoſtles hath braſte forthe makynge lawes ſeuerally lawes whole cōmunaltyes decreynge clargye exempted cyuyle lawes bryngynge cauſynge cyuyle ſcyſme dyuyſyon pluralyte cheyfe gouernours whiche haue ſhewed xvii chapytre fyrſte dyccion impoſſyble quyetnes tranquylite men alledgynge ſure vndoubted experyence therof ſayd pluralyte hedes hygheſt gouernours rote begynnynge peſtylence dyſtruccyon empyre italy whiche rote hurtes occaſyons euyls hathe cauſe vndoyng italye ſprōge dothe come forth durynge ſame ſhall neuer ceaſe cyuyle dyſcordes ſame empyre byſſhop rome hath longe tyme holden powre wherunto crope lytle lytle preuy preuary cacyon cuſtome rather abuſe furthermore fearynge leaſt ſame powre ſhulde reuoked hym emperour without cauſe exceſſes cōmytted hym wycked dylygence forbyddeth letteth treaſon creacyon promotynge emperour rome laſte one hathe braſte forthe ſo great boldnes hath decree expreſſed emperour rome bounde hym othe fydelyte beynge ſubiecte hym coactyue iuryſdyccyon appereth euydently lyfte ſhameles chyldren loke vpon folyſſhe vtterly deſpyſe worthy vii boke theyr narracyons whiche call decretalles tytle deſentencia et indicata whiche raſſhe myſaduyſed preſumpcyon moſte chryſten emperoure cōmēdacion henry viii emperour rome cauſe moſt cruel depoſycyon man vertues ſyngulerly amōge pryncꝭ approuyd tyme place ſtate happye worſhypfull memorye henry viii refuſynge agre faynynge hym ſelfe haue forgotten othe made dyſcrybed tranſgreſſoure certayne leſſe falſe preſumptuouſe narracyon called decretall whoſe tytle de iure iurando whiche neuertheles myght worthelye intyteled de iniuſta iniuria et illata dino imperatori ſuiſ que ſucceſſoribꝰ et affinibus omnibus contumelia ſaye wrongfull iniurye contumelye tytle iure iurādo dyſworſhyp done moſte honorable godly emperour ſucceſſours alyaunce maker canon lawe pronounced perſon defamed euyll name becauſe counte periured whiche alſo haue gone aboute ſpotte defyle famouſe memory hym yf myght haue ben ſpotted blemyſſhed wordes wrytynges ſuch falſe wrongfull accuſers dyſprayſers yet byſſhop rome theyr cardynals durſte call theſe oblygarchicall ordynacions appertaynyng powre theyr owne ſelues beynge fewe nōbre name lawes called decretalles albeit ſame intende bynde men vnto payne ſtate preſent world powre coactyue lykewyſe pryncꝭ worlde entende theyr lawes cauſe durſt expreſſe begynnynge ye name lawes fered reſyſtence correccyon aforſayd pryncꝭ treaſon ſo doynge cōmytted agaynſt prynces gouernours ¶ agayn ſpyrytual lawes named iura canonica ſaye canon lawes hereby note crafte deuyll begynnynge called ſuche maner ordynacyons iura canonica ende yt coloure worde though wyckedly aplyed ſhuld accompted taken antentyke myght imprynte bylefe reuerence obedyence ſayd ordynacyōs largely chryſten men hertes conclude togyther byſſhops rome conuayenge ſelues lytle lytle preuylye preched openly ſyxe latter ſygnyfycacions fulnes powre alſo ſelues cōmyttynge many mōſtruous thynges cyuyle ordre agaynſt lawe god man agaynſt ryght iudgement man hath reaſon ¶ howe maner byſſhop rome hathe vſed prymacye taken vpon hym fulnes powre ſpecyall within eccleſyaſtycall lymytes orderynge preeſtes xxiiij chapytre aforeſayd determynacyons foloweth conſequentlye ſhewe faſcyon byſſhops rome hath taken ſayd full powre vnto ſeues hath vſed doth vſe hetherto lykelyhode wyl vſe hereafter yf ſtopped letted fyrſt howe haue vſed inſtytucyon eccleſyaſtycall offycers dyſtrybutynge eccleſiaſtycall temporalles benefyces well vnto eccleſyaſtical mynyſtres vnto myſerable perſones whoſe cauſe alſo eccleſyaſtycal temporalles hath ben gyuen ordayned ſo dyſtributed dyſpoſed mynyſtres churche afterwardꝭ ſhewed haue vſed hetherto doth vſe hereafter wyll vſe theſe powres cōparyſon vnto lyue cyuylie aſ well prynces theyr ſubiectes byſſhops rome beynge permytted ſuffered hetherto nowe adayes worke accordyng fulnes powre hathe infected corrupted myſtycall bodye chryſte haue dymynyſſhed corrupted fynally maner haue vtterly deſtroyed taken awaye eleccyon whiche beſte waye ye moreouer whiche way onely ſecuryte well inſtytutynge maner offycer notwithſtandynge eleccion apoſtles multitude chryſten men made inſtytucion deacon vi chapytre actes haue dymynyſſhed fyrſte tournynge eleccyon clargye alone ought done chryſten prynces haue corrupted alſo dymynyſſhynge tranſlatynge ye auctoryte electynge byſſhop vnto certayne yonge men vnlerned vnſkylled lawe god call canon haue alſo maner vtterly deſtroyed byſſhops rome reſerue īmedyatlye theyr owne powre inſtytucion al eccleſiaſticall prelacyes dygnytes onely theſe alſo meane ſmaller offyces whiche maye agree belonge pure laye men cuſtody tēples church colleccyon dyſtrybucyon temporalles benefyces ordayned appoynted ſayd offycers whiche reſeruacyon decree determyne maner eleccions ſuffycyēt approued perſones voyde ſtrength though neuer ſo dewely made inſtytutynge ſtede theſe ſuffycyēt perſones fulnes theyr powre call beynge ignoraunte corrupted money prayer hatred loue feare pleaſure ſeruyce done optayne fauoure churche erre throughe ſome croked affeccyon perſons ignoraunte vnſkylled ſcrypture god fooles boyes without lernynge moſte parte men corrupte mynde openly knowen vycious leude dyſpoſed perſons whiche alſo ſpeake language tonge people made ouerſeers gouernours beynge ſtraunge nacyon wherfore let pope make anſwere chryſte x iohn̄ whiche pope agaynſt true eleccyon ought made amonge monſtruous thynges hath done dothe hath inſtytuted two byſſhops owne nacyon language one byſſhop wyncheſtre englande byſſhop londe denmarke whiche neyther ſpeake language whiche people theyr dyoceſis vnderſtande maner perſones ſame learnynge maners appertayneth nedeth reherce albeit byſſhop londe openly knowen denmarke churche dyoceſe beynge ſpoyled robbed droues great beaſtes neceſſarye huſbandrye tyllage grounde accordynge countree requyreth gatherynge great treaſures vnto hym ſelfe ſale forſakynge churche fled thenſe retourned owne regyon countree ſaye let byſſhop rome make anſwere howe paſtor byſſhop ſhall call owne ſhepe name knowynge maners conuerſacion howe ſhal ſhepe folowe hym vnderſtandynge knowynge voyce preachynge doctryne neyther nedefull nowe begge deſyre byſſhops curate puynces becauſe neceſſyte lacke men olde tymes englande men excellent good lyfe cōnynge holy doctryne whiche beynge vnſkylled language alſo beynge doctoure dyuynyte onely beynge lawyer pleader cauſes made gouernoure ouerſeer vnto ſo lykewyſe denmarke prouynces many open teſtymonyes myght brought lyke errour paſſe ouer becauſe ſpede ſhortnes wyll meruayle wondre ſe yonge men ignoraūte ſcryptures god lackynge alſo conuenyent grauyte maners men without experyence learnynge otherwhyles openlye dyffamed perſons made byſſhops promoted hygheſt dygnytyes offyces churche throughe symonye requeſt prayer great men ſaye otherwhyles throughe feare great men ſeruyce done cauſe cōſanguynyte affynyte ye doctours dyuynyte teacher holy ſcrypture men approued ye honeſtye theyr lyfe cōuerſacyon beynge put bye regarded whether theſe fayned falſe thynges ſpeake ſhall eaſyly perceyue whiche wyll reken vp byſſhoppes archebyſſhops prouynces patriatches inferyour prelate ſhal fynde one amonge x whiche doctoure dygynyte yt ſuffycyentlye learned holye ſcrypture whiche thynge ſhamed ſpeake althoughe dothe greue ſpeake becauſe true byſſhops theſe dayes neyther haue cōnynge preache people worde god neyther ſaye agaynſt erronyous doctrynes heretykes yf ſhall happen ryſe aforeſayd chaūces ſhamefully begge craue doctryne men notwithſtandynge doctoure gentyles paule doth ſaye thyrde chapytre fyrſte epyſtle timothe people chryſte byſſhop ought contende ſtryue temporalles accordynge counceyle chryſte apoſtles appereth x iohn̄ apoſtles wordes place afore alledged many place ſcrypture whiche leaue becauſe euydent ynoughe alſo abbreuacion proces tēporals inherytaunce apoſtles whiche lefte byſſhops theyr ſucceſſours ſaued kepte neyther emperyall dygnyties ſeculer domynyons ryght lybertyes ſpouſes chryſte ryghte c byſſhop rome nowe defende rather offende toke doubtfull intricate ſentence crafty ſophyſticall faſcyon moſte vniuſtlye hath anaū ced hym ſelfe agaynſt noble ludouyke cōmynge ye duke bauarye kynge romaynes wherfore barnarde iiii chapytre ye ſecōde boke wryten eugenius de conſideratione whan ſpoken dylygent cure charge ſoules church apoſtles lefte theyr ſucceſſours ſayth wyſe thynge hath apoſtles lefte ſayde haue gyue thynge one thynge knowe golde ſyluer within lytle ſame bernarde ſayth ſo thou mayſte chalenge theſe thynges wyt tēporalles vnto thy ſelfe whatſoeuer waye tytle one thynge aſſured ryght tytle apoſtle agayne afterwardes whiche ſaythe bernarde gaue wyt dylygent cure charge haue ſayde vpon church concernynge domynyon lordſhyppe ſayde barnarde ſayth afterwardes hathe gyuen domynyon lordſhyppe ſayde hym ſelfe beynge lordes hauynge domynyon clargye beynge made example flocke becauſe thou ſhalte thynke haue ben ſpoken onely humylyte alſo truth theſe wordes chryſt hym ſelfe goſpell ruler gentyles hath domynyon vpon whiche haue powre ouer called benefycyall foloweth afterwardes ſhall ſo playne euydent domynyon lordſhyp vtterly forbydden apoſtles ye thynge whiche worthye moſte meruaylynge moſte marked regardyd men redreſſed broughte agayne dewe forme maner prynces beynge mynyſtres god inſtytucyon byſſhoppe rome byſſhoppes ſeldome dyuyne choſen byſſhoppe rome moſte parte one taken companye lawyer pleders cauſes whiche thynge vtterlye contrarye ſcryptures god dyſagreynge ryght reaſon moſt ſhameful thynges face church alſo conuenyently leſſe maner marked concernynge company cardynalles vnto dygnyte taken wanten yonge men many learned ſkylled holy ſcryptures notwithſtandynge byſſhop rome churche colledge ought example vnto theſe thynges thus farforth beit ſpoken retournynge purpoſe wherof ſpake let v ſay yt byſſhop rome fulnes powre doth gyue greatter multytude greateſt meane ſmaleſteſt dygnytyes eccleſyaſtycall promocyons vnlearned men ignoraunte holy ſcryptures wolde god gaue crymynous perſones aſ well thoſe knowen hym ſelfe thoſe knowen chyldren infantes alſo throughe ſymony outher theyr owne partye y• intreaters ſome corrupte affeccyon moſte partye greateſt moſte pryncypall ſeates beynge thus infected promotynge yea alſo intruſyon ſuche maner perſones al ſmaller cure offyces belongynge gyfte alſo throughe cōtagyouſnes made corrupte poyſoned beynge glad lyke perſōs vnto ſelues euer lyke glad lyke man man horſe horſe gentyle phyloſopher ſayde ſet vpon gate ſymonye ſome vnlawfull waye whiche ſelues entred came eccleſyaſtical offyces vnto vnlerned perſons lewde maners wyllynge accordynge theyr owne maners whiche maners dygnyte hath chaunged often tymes hathe ſhewed brought lyght hate reiecte eſchewe oppreſſe holye ryghttuous learned men whiche go aboute entre houſe god ſuche maner pathes beynge enemyes vnto ſelues chryſte whiche imortall trouthe ſaythe euyll doth hateth lyght ouerhyppe alſo aforeſayde byſſhop purchaſe get loue fauoure thākes great men peraduenture alſo money receyued beſyde hathe promoted certayne yonge men vnto byſſhoppes famouſe cyties notwithſtandynge haue ben ignoraunte vnſkylled law god dyſcyplynes ſcyences moreouer promoted holye ordre yet ſaynt iherome ſayth euandre preeſt hode contayned offyce byſſhop ouerſeer eccleſyaſtycall gouernours beynge thus infected doubtles whole myſtycall bodye chryſte ſycke dyſeaſed whan prelate church omytteth leaueth exhortacyons obſecracyons increpacyons curate accordynge holſome doctryne dothe cōmytte deteſtable abhomynable thynges openlye people offended taketh occaſyon ſynnynge throughe example marke ſet vp ſhoters ſo ſet example people whiche thynge chryſte conſyderynge ſayd v mathewe lette lyght ſo ſhyne ſyghte men maye ſe good workes hereof cōmeth rote fyrſte peruerſyte maners vſed nowe adayes vnto whiche inconcluſyon foloweth eternall dampnacyon chryſte ſaythe v mathewe yf blynde man guyde blynde man bothe fall dyche ſhall ſaye dyſtrybucyon beſtowynge temporalles reſydue ſayd temporalles ſuperfluouſe ſuffyce neceſſytie eccleſyaſtycall mynyſtres ought dyſtrybuted vnto poore impotent beggers myſerable perſons euery man maner doth knowe nowe ar turned ſhameful vſes ſpeake truely ſhameful abuſes vnto newe kynd almoſe one moſte parte ſayde temporalles ſpente beſtowed vpon men warre horſemen foreman rayſe vp noryſſhe contynuall warres amonge chryſten people laſte maye ſubdewe make ſubiectes theyr owne tyrannycall powre thus aforeſayde thynges appereth euydent reaſon fulnes powre myſtycall body churche touchynge matter pryncypall mēbers ſpecyallye cauſe example prelate euery ſyde infected nere corrupcyon ¶ nowe ſpeake forme faſcyon body whiche forme ought cō ſyſte ordre dewe ſytuacyon mēbres ſame dody hym yt luſte dylygently beholde aduyſe marke well ſhall ſeme euyll fauored myſſhapen monſtre man wolde iudge bodye yt beaſt ſimilitude myſſhapen vnprofytable cōuenyent operacions whiche body euery one mēbres therof īmedyatly ioyned knytte vn heed ye fynger hande yf ioyned knytte īmedyatly vnto heed becauſe wanteth due place ſhall want alſo vertue conuenyent mouynge operacyon ſhall ſo yf fynger ioyned hande hande arme arme ſholder ſholder necke necke knytte heed conuenyēt ioyntes ſo body made comly ſhap ſo heed maye ſende cōuenyent vertue mēbres one accordynge nature ordre ſayd membres ye reaſon hereof may operacions cōuenyent belongynge vnto ſelues whiche forme maner ought regarde euerye bothe eccleſiaſticall alſo cyuyle regyment gouernaunce byſſhop rome īmedyatly beholde loke vpon ſyngulare pertyculare actes euery pertyculare perſone prouynces īmedyatlye dyrecte yf theſe thynges ſhulde done ſuffycyently accordyngly ought holpen ſpecyall mynyſtres accordynge due ordre body churche beynge ſo ordred may contynue alſo encreaſe whiche thynge paule doctor gentyles perceyuynge ſayde wyſe iiii chapytre epheſyans let v growe hym whiche poyntes heed chryſte whome whole body beynge cō pacted knytte togyther euery ioynte ſubmynyſtracyon accordynge operacyon euery parte meaſure maketh increaſe bodye fulnes powre permytted vnto byſſhop rome ordre dewe forme taken awaye alſolueth prelate archebyſſhops byſſhoppes chaptours collegyes abbottes freers monkes pryours relygyous houſes theyr allegiās due vnto theyr prynce hath ſubdued al theſe owne cure īmedyate correccyon euydent profyte vtylyte rather openly knowen greadynes deſyre hepe ſutes ſtryues lawe vnto hym ſelfe gatherynge money ſpoylynge robbynge prelate alſo intendynge greatter ſubduynge yet howe great inſolencie pryde hath folowed therof maner euery man knoweth theſe aforeſayd perſons lackynge cure obedyence dewe theyr prynce made ſtubburne dyſobedyent without reuerence drede whome ought ryght worthelye ſubiectes obedyent taketh alſo hereof vnto ſelues occaſyon lybertie ſyn large adde newe ſprynge braunche ſayd rote yt byſſhop rome fulnes powre hath forbydden whiche haue eccleſiaſticall benefyce euer without lycence make teſtamentes hath decreed goodes dyeth inteſtate cōuayed brought īmedyatlye vnto ſee adde alſo greatter thynge deuyll moſt large ſymonye althoughe fulfylled deade ſame powre reſerueth rente profytes frutes benefyces whatſoeuer place fyrſte yere ar vacante gatheryng maner vnto hymſelfe treaſures worlde robbynge kyngdoms prouynces ſame whiche prouynces ought dyſtrybuted mynyſtres goſpell myſerable perſons elles turned ſubſydie ſuccour cōmune wealthe wherof taken yf nede ſhall requyre herefore haue ben ordayned aſſygned agayne ītollerable thynge ſayth legacyes bequeſtꝭ teſtamentes chryſten laye men paſſage beyonde ſee cauſes accordynge dyſpoſycion certayne determynate perſones whome call cōmyſſaryes dothe appertayne ordrynge ſame fulnes powre meruayle hereof ſeynge yt certayne byſſhop amonge hath ſayd hymſelfe hath domynyon kynges prynces realmes cōmunyties notwithſtandynge yt dede none aforeſayd thynges doth appertayne vnto powre ſame rote mo greuouſer thynges theſe ſhall chaunce ſprynge vp whiche tolde ſo dyuers nature one inconuenyent graunted namely ſuche one whiche incōuenyencꝭ may thought ymagyned aboute cyuyle actes cō tayned harde thynge inconuenyences whatſoeuer chaūce accordynge gentyle phyloſopher aryſtotle full powre beynge due vnto hym foloweth may whatſoeuer helyſte wherfore doth ſuſpende dyſanulle reuoke ye ordynaciōs lawes men owne pleaſure thynge beynge extreme vttermoſte incōuenyent yt may worldly regyment gouernaunce well ſayntꝭ phyloſophers hath hated refuſed proued demōſtracyon xi chapytre fyrſt dyccyon alſo largely confyrmed v dyccion auctoryte ſaynt auguſtyne ye vi chapytre fyrſt epyſtle timothe fulnes powre permytted vnto hym yt whole body ye churche infectyd ordre eccleſiaſtycall iconomie broken cyuyle regyment gouernaunce letted vtterly troubled parte vpon whiche byſſhop yf chryſten men wyll caſte theyr iyes beſeche whiche hath ben duſked bleared many adaye moſt parte certayne couer cloke coloure ſophiſtycall honeſty ſhallſe clerely ſelues ſoeuer hath viſyted courte rome ſaye truely houſe marchaundyſe horryble denne theues vſe chryſtes wordes whoſoeuer hath viſyted ſhal learne reporte great many credyble perſons yt made maner receptacle ſanctuarye myſcheuous men marchauntes bothe ſpyrytuall temporall thynge concourſe ſymonyacall perſons countrees thynge bablynge noyſe proctours pleader cauſes aſſaulte quarelers falſe accuſers vexacion iuſte men iuſtyce innocēt perſons ioperdy leaſt wyſe ſo greatly dyfferred put yf notable bye money laſte beynge clene beggarde theyr money conſumed themſelues weryed innumerable labour compelled gyue ouer theyr ryghtful myſerable cauſes lawes men thundre ſounde lowde lawe doctryne god outher kepeth ſcylence elles ſoundeth ſeldome treatyſes rolles rentalles preuy caſtes deuyſed inuade prouynces chryſten men violence powre armes get take away ſayd prouynces whoſe cuſtody haue ben lawfully cōmytted howe get wyn ſoules thought care counſayles moreouer none ordre cō tynuall horroure inhabyteth dwelleth whiche haue ben preſent ſeen maner thynke mynde ſe terryble dredefull image whiche nabugodonozor dyd ſe dreame recyted interpre tacyon image whiche danyell deſcrybeth ſeconde chapytre danyell hauynge heed golde armes breſte ſyluer bely thyghes braſſe legges yerne one parte fete yerne erthe thynge betokeneth great image ſtate courte rome pope whiche olde tyme terrible lewde euyll men nowe horryble beholde vnto good vertuous men ſuperyoure mēbres image heed y• breſte armes thynge ſyght affeccyon loue golde ſyluer workes man handes bely thyghes thynge great noyſe ſounde ſeculare ſtryfes cauſes falſe accuſacyons quarelles ſymonyacall byenges ſellynges wyll nowe ſpeake thundres lyghtnynges curſes excōmunycacions wryten gyuen forth mouthe agaynſt chryſten men whiche refuſe thoughe ryghtuouſlye ſeculerlye ſubiected vnto byſſhop rome churche gyue temporal goodes vnto beſeche tell thyngis thyghes braſſe pompouſe proude ordynaūcꝭ pleaſures ryote wel nere alvanyties yea ſuch vnſemelye laye men pompous ordynaunce imprynte ſences men whiche ought example chaſtyte honeſtye vnto legges yerne fete toe wherupon image ſtandeth made faſt beynge partlye erthe towardes thynge go vſurpacyon inuaſyon occupacion ſeculare domynyons kyngdoms prouynces vyolent powre armed men men harnayſed yerne bryngynge purpoſe ſuperyoure membres wyt geuynge golde ſyluer whiche prouoketh armed men vnto alſo bryngynge braſen bely thyghes theyr lewde promyſe ſuche thynges vocale abſolucyon thoughe dyſceytful ſynnes paynes iniuſte condempnacyon curſynge thoughe throughe godes defence doth hurte whiche defendeth theyr owne lybertye wyllynge obſerue theyr faythe allegyaunce dewe theyr prynces gouernours ſoles fete toe beynge molde erthe reaſon therof brytle eaſy breke thynge repreſente vnconſtancye vnſtablenes courte rome thynge ſygnyfye betoken feblenes ye occaſyōs becauſe wyll ſaye falſytie iniquyte euydently knowen men vpon occaſyons pope rome groundeth hymſelfe wherunto leaneth agaynſt faythfull people chryſte oppreſſe ſame prophet doth wytneſſe recorde vpon image ſhall fall ſtone cut hyll without handes ſay kynge whome god ſhall rayſe vp elected grace vnyuerſyte men wyt gyuynge hym powre whoſe kyngdom ſhall gyuen kynge ſaye vertue grace trynyte worke powre yt hādes men ſhal fyrſt cruſſhe breke ye earthy part terryble horryble monſtruouſe image wyt fete vpon ſtandeth vnconuenyently wyt cauſynge falſe vniuſte cauſes baulde occaſyons may call truely poetet knowen vnto prynces people ſopheme dyſceyte beynge opened dyſcloſed impungned humayne demonſtracyons dyſtroyed anulled veryties holy ſcrypture afterwarde ſhall breake yerne partꝭ ſame puttynge awaye cruell wycked powre conſequently ſhall cauſe braſen partes wyt auctoryte curſynge whiche hath preſumptuouſly taken vpon hym vpon people prynces troublous noyſe ſtryfe ſeculare iuryſdyccyons vſurped conſequentlye cauſes vexacyons kepe ſylence dombe exceſſes ſuperfluyties voluptuous pleaſures pompes vanyties ceaſe laſt ſhall ſubdue dyſtroye golde ſyluer ſame image wyt couytouſnes robberye byſſhop rome ſo accordynge mynde aforeſayd profyte yerne earth braſſe golde ye ſyluer ſayd image ſhall broken al togyther ſay vyces exceſſes aboueſayde courte ſhal quenched dyſtroyed ſtrawes brente vnto aſſhes caryed awaye wynde thynge whiche bothe agaynſt nature agaynſt lawe bothe god man contrary al reaſon thynge longe abyde cōtynewe ¶ howe maner byſſhop rome hathe vſed aforeſayd maners fulnes powre ineſpecyall without eccleſiaſtical lymytes towardes laye men towardes cyuyle temporall thynges xxv chapytre nowe remayneth vnto v ſearche maner facyon thynges byſſhops rome haue vſed hytherto vſe fulnes powre whiche haue taken vnto ſelues without eccleſiaſticall lymytes yet wyl fyrſt make reherſall call remembraunce vſage cuſtomes prymatyue churche procedynge ſame euen begynner heed therof whiche chryſte fyrſte promoter ſetters forwarde therof holy apoſtles wytte chryſte cam chryſte taught worlde teache alſo exercyſe offyce preeſte paſtor feder ſoules beynge interpretoure expounder lawe fyrſte byſſhop rome poſſeſſed landes rome red haue ben fyrſt vntyll tyme churche colledge preeſtꝭ lyued maner chryſtes lyfe apoſtles wyt obſeruynge meretor yous moſt hyghe perfyte pouertie albeit peraduenture aforeſayd orbane dyd thynge pryncypally may iudge intent cherytably maye beſte pytie ſuccurrynge releuynge poore people mercye yet yf toke vnto hym ſelfe powre chalenge ſuche maner landes prouentꝭ rente therof afore coactyue iudge yf powre auctoryte ſell ſayde landꝭ dyſtrybute pryce vnto poore folke dyd ſell dyſtrybute whether dyd wyllyngly ignoraunce doubteles declyned ſwarued moſt hyghe pouertie aforeſayd ſtate perfeccion whiche maner alſo many byſſhops rome dyd folowe thynge vntyll tyme conſtantyne whiche ſpace tyme byſſhoppes rome theyr colledge made vnto ſelues certayne ordynacyons concernynge ceremonyes cuſtomes eccleſiaſtical aboute deuyne ſeruyce honeſt ſtate colledge company preeſtes ſame ordynacyons beynge profytable dyd cōmunycate vnto church namely ſuche note agayne requyred dyd alſo take vpon ſelues pytie charytie cure dylygence church worlde accordynge theyr poſſybylytie becauſe often tymes wanted ſuffyciēt gouernours poſtors prelate therfore dyd exhorte monyſſhe coūſayle perſons church thoſe thynges whiche appertayned honeſtye fayth beleue church thankefully kyndly wyllyngly receyued ye exhortacyons monyciōs whiche church alſo whan otherwhyles ſome preeſtꝭ byſſhops ſome deacōs perſons frowarde dyd ceaſe troblynge touchynge maners fayth brotherlye monycion preſente peraduenture thoſe perſones whiche moſte dyſcrete amonge wyllynge lyue godly vertuouſlye chryſte procured excōmunycacyons curſes gyuen howe excō munycacyōs cam fyrſte rome byſſhoppe rome churche whoſe monycyons chryſtened people moſte feared cauſes aforeſayde agaynſt rebellyous perſones dyſtroublers men otherwyſe crymynouſe perſones elles byſſhops rome dyd theyr owne accorde vndeſyred zele loue fayth therfore chryſten people whiche place moſt parte agreed obeye byſſhop rome churche conſeruacyon vnytie faythe quyetnes amonge ſelues one becauſe theſe ſayde thynges coulde kepte powre coactyue cōuenyēt way moch yt tyme ye humayne lawemakers maner prynces euery hethen chryſtened whan tyme conſtantyne fyrſte emperourr rome howe councelles fyrſt congregated gathered come whiche fyrſte emperoures permytted graūted chryſten people myght aſſemble come togyther openly fyrſte made general councelles preeſtes byſſhopes cōmaundement auctoryte forſayd emperour whiche councelles doubtefull ſences holy ſcrypture defyned determyned true ſences ſame ſequeſtred dyſceuered falſe erronyous ſences whiche falſe corrupte madde ſences ſome preeſtes otherwhyles throughe ignoraunce moſte cōmunelye throughe ſuperſtyciouſnes malyce ſowen ſparpled abrode amonge chryſtes faythfull people whiche councelles alſo ordynacyons ſtatutes made aboute eccleſiaſticall vſage cuſtomes concernynge deuyne ſeruyce honeſtye good ordre deacon preeſtꝭ touchynge promotynge vnto eccleſiaſticall offyces well ſeperable whiche call ordres ſeperable whiche call prelacyes cure office ſeꝑable inſeperable ſoules ſuch offyces incertayne place prouynces alſo cō cernynge dyſtrybucyon temporalles benefyces oblacions thynges gyuen vnto moueables vnmoueables mynyſterynge goſpell forme maner determyned ſette appoynted ſayde councelles whiche forme maner obſerued kepte prynce gouernour gaue made coactyue precepte lawe byndynge euery maner man bothe preeſtes laye men payne punyſſhement outher reall perſonall done vnto tranſegreſſours accordynge euery one dyd require ye ſtate ye ſtate preſent world canony call lawes fyrſt made agaynſt preeſtes agaynſte laye men ſuch maner lawes made agaynſt preeſtꝭ biſſhops thā agaynſt men becauſe cōmunelye tyme preeſtes whiche gaue cauſe makynge ſuche coactyue preceptes lawes neyther byſſhops rome neyther byſſhoppes euer dyd reſyſte ſpeke agaynſt humayne lawe maker prynce beynge ſubiectꝭ ye lawes ſtatutes prynces alwayes made ſupply cacyons prynces wolde make ſuch lawes appereth aforſayd boke iſodorye approued hyſtoryes ¶ moreouer ſame prynces emperours lawes made hath ben made concernynge certayne nombre ſhuld preeſtes accordynge prouynces concernynge temporall goodes belongnnge moueables vnmoueables whiche hath ben gyuen ſayd thē ſayd conſtantyne emperours rome prynces gouernours falſely fayned ſucceſſyuely alſo ſome ſynguler perſones agayne concernynge cyuyle contencious actes albeit ſayd lawes hath ben moderated ſpecyall fauours grace goodnes humayne law maker prynces conſyderynge regardynge dygnyte reuerence ordre preeſthode becauſe accordynge truthe offyce chryſte repreſented regardynge alſo grauyte theyr maners ſymplycyte innocencye parſones whiche tyme mynyſters goſpell pryuyleges preſtꝭ bare ſayd offyce euen lyke actes ordayned made leſſe rygorous lawes laye men grauntynge vnto alſo many pryuyleges tyme nombre fewe deuoute nowe many vndeuoute humylyte humblenes eaſylye geuynge place makynge reſyſtence aſſaultes lawyer pleader cauſes ſtrengthed compaſed aboute ben nowe euery ſyde vyolent armed powre defence ſelues offendynge hurtynge olde tyme great abhomynacyon ſhulde haue ſemed cyuyle monſtre yf clarkes namely preeſtes byſſhops taken harnes weaponed ſelues cōmaūded men take harneys fyght wherfore ſaynt ambroſe place afore alledged ix chapytre dyccyon ſayth thus ſhall ambroſe armure preeſtes able maye ſory maye wepe maye wayle ſyghe teares armoure weapon agaynſt warres ſoldyers alſo agaynſt gothes ſuche thynges munymentes ſtrength aydes preeſte otherwyſe thus neyther ought neyther maye reſyſte cauſe neded tyme ſpecyall fauours pryuylegies myght lyue nowe ye contrary nedeth quyetlye ſafelye myght eſcape vexacyons quarelles falſe accuſarers howbeit nowe adayes conuerſyon chaunge made thynge reſpecte comparyſon laye men contrarye qualytye olde tymes lyued vnder lawes cyuyle ordynacyons ſeculer prynces longe ſeaſon whole colledge companye marke ye prynces leſe hono• regall preeſtes toke ſame prynces people gyftes confyrmaciōs inueſtytures theyr offyces prelacyes cure lyke elles ſmaller offyces alſo powre dyſtrybute beſtowe temporalles benefyces neyther dyd byſſhops rome olde tyme ſtryue agaynſt emperours rome cauſe ſuche maner ſubieccyons neyther agaynſt people ꝑtyculer perſons beynge patrones church knewe bounde ſubieccyon lawe god alſo lawe man haue ſhewed ſuffycyentlye ſcrypture polityke reaſons iiii v viii xvii dyccyon ſo reade symachus beynge man sarde byrthe nacion beynge coelected one lawrence dyſcorde confyrmed pope rome iudgement whiche theodorichus kynge made dyd gyue alſo wryteth martyne ſaynt gregorye gregorye ſaythe martyne choſen pope mauricius ye emperour confyrmeth hym letter emperyall alſo byſſhops rome wonte deſyre confyrmacyon theyr pryuylegies humbly emperours red vitelliane whiche syguen borne vitellianus papa conſtantyne whiche syryane borne many byſſhops rome yea moreouer wonte go perſonallye vnto emperoures cōſtātyne pope place farre dyſtaūte theſe ſupplycacyons theyr confyrmacyons obtayned red many cronycles approued hyſtoryes alſo whiche greatter thynge iohn̄ xii depoſed poynt wold broughte agayne iohn̄ xii pope depoſed otto pray god mayeſe ſuch thyngꝭ agayne lāde otherwhere popeſhyp demerytes ſo requyrynge otto fyrſte beynge emperour people conſentynge therunto clargy alſo laye men alſo cronycle martyne ſpeaketh benedicte ix red two elected contenciouſlye depoſed emperyal cenſure iudgement henry whiche emperour rome ſame pryncypall cheyfe auctoryte appertayneth depoſe deſtytute thynge yf ſhall expedyent whiche belongeth inſtytute aſmoche euery byſſhop ought elected prynce auctoryte ſame may deſtytuted depoſed hath ben certyfyed xvii dyccion ¶ byſſhops rome therfore prouynces preeſtes colledge companye clarkes lyued example chryſte apoſtles vnder coactyue iuryſdyccyon gouernaunce whiche prynces ruler throughe entyſement pryckynge prynce worlde fyrſte father pryde ambycyon ſuggeſture putter mynde vyces deuyll certayne byſſhoppes rome deduced nay rather ſeduced brought way chryſt apoſtles clene contrary way auaryce couetouſnes inuadynge cōmynge myndes dyd thruſte thenſe ye hygheſt merytoryouſe ꝑfyte pouertie chryſte plāted ſet churche agayne pryde ambycyon deſyre honoure ſeculare domynyon inuadynge cōmynge vpon ſame hath dryuen thenſe moſte hyghe perfyte humylyte whiche chryſte cōmaunded charged obſerued kepte ſame clergy vnyuerſall cōpanye preeſtꝭ amonge whiche byſſhoppes one simplicius tibertinus byſſhoppe rome red simplicius tibertinus one ye fyrſte traytours biſſhoppes rome haue ben fyrſte ſuffered thynge simplicius takynge hym auctoryte wotte neuer whenſe albeit knowe certaynely excepte excuſed ignoraunce wherof toke raſſhe myſauyſed preſumpcyon ordayned decreed clarke ought take inueſtiture lay man vnderſtādynge meanynge inueſtiture benefyces offyces haue ſpoken tofore albeit yet ſtatute decree euydently ſygnyfyed predeceſſours wyllynge gyue dewe humylyte inueſtiture reuerēce prynces emperours wonte receyue aforeſayd inueſtytures laye men agayne ſucceſſoure thoughe nexte hym pelagius fyrſte name ordayned decreed heretykes good honeſt man gaue ye emperour pygge owne ſo ſhuld punyſſhed ſeculer powres offycers ſtatute decree alſo marueyled aſmoche knewe well ynoughe ſuche lawe made agaynſt heretykes tyme iuſtiniane emperoure rome becauſe belongeth auctorytye make ſuche maner lawes byſſhop vnleſſe peraduenture thynge ben graū ted hym auctoryte temporall prynce therfore lykewyſe simplicius aforeſayd dyd ſo alſo dyd pelagius put ſyeth mannes corne vſurpynge auctoryte vnto hym ſelfe whiche appertayned vnto adriane ye iii pope worſhypfull p̄late warraunt man whome agayne adryane thyrde ſucceded though imedyatlye ſayd vſurpacyon ordayned decreed none emperoure ſhulde intromytte medle concernynge eleccyon pope maye vſe wordes ſayde martyne whiche ſtatute decree beynge vtterlye ſtrengthe aſmoche made hym lacked auctoryte make ſuche maner lawes dyd contayne alſo open inconuenyence hathe benſhewed ye mayeſe yt writer hiſtories truſted tymes man may ſoone deceyued excepte haue ryghte iudgement fyrſt ſcrypture martin freer begger xviii chapitre dyccyon beſyde contrarye ben roborated eſtablyſſhed longe laudable cuſtome albeit martyne doth ſay maketh mencion leo x yt romayns lewde wronge cuſtome deſyred byſſhop gyuen vnto emperour confeſſeth haue ben cuſtome graunte ſayd truthe owne auctoryte calleth lewde croked cuſtome intendynge therby iuſtyfye aforeſayd vſurpaciōs byſſhops rome deface auctoryte lawes emperours goynge aboute pleaſe man rather pleaſe god truth ſayth falſely vntruly ſheweth playnelye begynnynge myſterye thynge haue ben ſhyt vp cloſed hym ſelfe neyther credence gyuen vnto martyne behalfe ordre partaker ſuche maner vſurpacyon ordres whiche call beggynge freets haue optayned beleue haue optayned byſſhops rome exempcyon wyt poynte ſubiectes vnder iuryſdyccyon theyr owne paſtores byſſhops ſuperyoure prelate ¶ nowe retourne wherof ſpake lewde vnlaudable cuſtome byſſhops churche rome inſtytuted emperours haue ſayd rede alſo whiche laboure ſayd martyne cō trarye agaynſt truthe confeſſe graunte auctorite larger maner aforeſayde hathe afterwardes ben graunted charlemayne otto fyrſt kynge almayne emperour rome ye people rome byſſhop clargye ſeculer perſons wherfore red approued hyſtoryes true alſo decree folowynge came forthe cōmune conſente people rome leo pope ſynodye whiche congregated rome church ſaynt ſauyoure accordynge example blyſſed adryane byſſhop apoſtolyke ſee whiche graūted vnto lorde charles moſt vyctoryous kynge fraūce lombardy dygnyte ſenatour ordynacyon inueſtyture apoſtolyke ſee alſo leo ſeruaunte ſeruauntes god byſſhop clargye people rome conſtytute confyrme roborate apoſtolyke auctoryte graunte gyue otto fyrſte kynge almayne ſucceſſours realme empyre italye foreuer well powre choſe ſucceſſoure vnto ſelfe alſo ordayne aſſygne byſſhop apoſtolyke ſee alſo ordayne arche byſſhops byſſhoppes ſo ſhall take theyr inueſtiture hym theyr conſecracion ought take onely theſe excepted whome emperour hathe graunted pope archebyſſhops man henſforth ſo meaneth byſſhops within ye emperours dominion el emperour hathe nought leccyon biſſhops englande punyſmēt wolde put vre steuen nicholas euer dygnytie relygyon holynes ſhall haue powre electe outher ſenatoure byſſhop hygheſt apoſtolyke ſee ordayne byſſhop ſoeuer without conſente ſayd emperoure whiche ſhall made without money ſhall ſenatour alſo kynge yf ſo chaunce byſſhop elected clargye excepte lauded alowed aforeſayde kynge haue inueſtyture hym let hym cōſecrated yf man enterpryſe go aboute thynge agynſt auctoryte haue decreed hym vnder excōmunycacion accurſed except ſhall repent punyſſhed perpetuall exyle banyſſhement el punyſſhed extreme punyſſhementꝭ deathe decree alſo steuē pope ſucceſſour vnto aforeſayd leo hath confyrmed alſo one nicholas ſucceſſour steuen cōmaūdynge obſerued kepte vnder payne terryble curſe wyt tranſgreſſours brekers oughte accompted amonge wycked men whiche ſhall ryſe agayne iudge ment profyte ſayth fyrſte pſalme decree ſpecyallye noted yt auctoryte concernynge inueſtytures whiche byſſhop rome whole people dyd tranſlate vnto emperour touchynge pope partye certayne renūcyacion fyrſt pryncypall auctoryte hereof appertaynynge emperour whiche graū ted pope auctoryte gyuynge ye inueſtyture vnto byſſhops arche byſſhops becauſe tēporall thynges whome ſoeuer ſhall haue ben tranſlated maner churche touchynge thynge ſubiecte prynce prouynce whiche ſayde temporalles ſytuate lyenge ſygnyfyed aforeſayde decree ſayde excepte thoſe whome emperoure hathe graunted pope archebyſſhoppe alſo inſtytute byſſhop apoſtolyke ſee appertayneth powre auctoryte emperour notwithſtandynge certayne byſſhops rome vſurpynge iuryſdyccyon people prynces aſwell makynge gyuynge lawes gyuen haue enterpryſed make promulgate publyſſhe theſe lawes thoughe vnduely wrongfully lytle lytle haue proceded gone forwarde namely emperyall ſee beynge vacante wherupon cōmenly moſt part occupacion certayne tēporalles ſo far may perceyued cronycles approued hyſtoryes ſtryfes haue ben rayſed vp betwene emperours pope rome howbeit biſſhops rome haue cauſed moche ſtryfe debate blode ſhedynge ſayd byſſhops haue done agaynſt councell precepte chryſt apoſtles whiche ought ſuccede apoſtles offyce preeſthode apoſtleſhyp ought alſo obſerue kepe moſte hyghe pouertie humylytie turnynge certayne waye contrarye ignoraūce malyce throughe bothe haue ſhewed tofore haue begon īmortall perpetuall contencion ſtryfe agaynſt ſayd emperours whiche ſame contencyon moſt amonge certayne byſſhop rome called paſchalis began agaynſt henry iiii kynge pope paſcal good man ſmall almayne hyſtoryes recorde ſayde byſſhop dyd prohybyte ſayd henry come vp vnto emperyall dygnyte reyſynge vp agaynſt hym people rome vntyll ſuch tyme aforeſayd henry beynge tuſky embaſſadours letter dyd graūte maner cōpulſyon vnto ye ſame byſſhop inueſtitures inſtytuciōs byſſhops abbottes clarkes whiche henry agayne aforeſayd pope requyrynge othe entred cytie concernynge thynges whiche extorted gotten hym cōpulſyon taken al colledge cardynalles cōcluſyon beynge delyuered peace aforeſayd emperour agaynſt rayſynge agayne olde ſtryfe moche ende laſte great laboures paynes ¶ martyne telleth aforeſayde emperour repentynge vſe wordes ſame martyne waxynge wyſe agayne frelye reſygned ſtaffe rynge one calyxte ſucceſſoure paſcall inueſtyture byſſhoppes calixte pope prelate graunted canonycall eleccyon ſhulde made church throughout whole empyre poſſeſſyones regalles ſaynt peter throughe diſcorde ſtryfe debate durſt non thynke yt freer martyne lyeth otto iiii emperoure churche ben alienated reſtored churche rome dyſpoſed ordred poſſeſſyons aſwell clarkes laye men occaſyon warre ben taken awaye ſhulde faythfullye trulye reſtored agayne whiche ſayd grauntes pryuyleges otto iiii frederyke ſeconde emperours rome afterwardes wyllynge laufull cauſe peraduenture reuoke reuokynge vtterlye el parte ſuffered many dyſceyptes perſecucyons impedymentes vexacyons byſſhoppes clargye rome ſome theyr predeceſſours haue ben holpen frederyke ye ſeconde people ſubiectes vnto reaſon rule regyment byſſhppes rome theyr offycers mynyſtres hath otherwhyles taſted peraduenture tyrannye haue ſayde hathe ben fyrſte pryncypall occaſyon noryſſher preſent ſtryfe dyſcorde betwene emperours pope rome enemyties dyſcordes behalfe emperoures prynces haue many tymes ben ceſſed vpon blynde zeale towarde lawe god feare elles myght taken heretykes rebellyons agaynſt holy churche men call clargye byſſhops rome wyll vnduelye exceſceſſyuely poſſeſſe temporall thynges vnder lawes ſtatutes decree emperours clene agaynſt example doctryne chryſt apoſtles hath ben ſhewed tofore notwithſtandynge oughte onely theſe thynges theyr owne alſo thyngꝭ beynge theyr owne rather gyue place contende ſtryue accordynge counſell whiche paule gyueth chryſten men vi chapytre corynthians ſayth thus one man amonge whiche may iudge betwene brother brother doth one brother ſtryue brother iudgement afore infydels truely ſo doynge ye declare ſynne reygne haue iudgemētꝭ betwene rather take wronge rather ſuffre hurte loſſe foloweth afterwardes angry ſame place whiche maye conuenyently ſayd well nere vnto byſſhops rome clarkes wronge worke dyſceypte chryſten brother knowe vniuſte perſones ſhall poſſeſſe kyngdome god begyled myſtake erre neytheyr fornycatours neyther worſhyppers imagies neyther adulterer neyther bouggardes vſynge ſynne ſodomytes neyther theues neyther couetous men neyther dronkerdes neyther euyll ſayers neyther extorcyoners robber ſhall poſſeſſe kyngdome god whiche ſayenge counſayle ſaynt paule byſſhops rome reſydue byſſhops clarkes lytle markynge regardynge yf tyme thynke ſelues greued emperours rome reaſon takynge tythes ſuch temporall trybutes ſuſtentacyon mayntaynynge theyr ſoldyers neceſſyte warre beynge towarde nere hande fauoure benefyte temporall thynges whiche haue receyued taken gracyouſlye gyuen vnto emperours rome beynge lyfted vp pryde ignoraunte theyr owne condycion eſtate moſt vnkynde vnkynde men certayne vnbrydeled preſumpcyon haue braſte forth horryble blaſphemyes curſynges aſwell agaynſt emperours agaynſt chryſten people ſubiectes vnto albeit ſayde curſes haue returned agayne vnto theyr owne wreched ſoules bodyes rather haue hurted emperours innocent flocke chryſten people ¶ beynge contented temporalles graunted vnto biſſhops rome ben thefes robber emperours throughe vnſacyable deſyre whiche haue vnto ſuche thynges haue vyolently entred vpon many temporall prouynces appertaynynge ryght emperoure temporalles cyties romandiole farrarie bononie alſo landes iuryſdyccyons ſpecyallye whan emperyall ſeate hathe ben vacante whiche thynge tyranny vſurpacyon vttermoſte inconuenyent cyuyle inconuenyentes haue made ſelues prynces lawmaker ende myght brynge kynges people theyr bondage moſt intollerable ſhamefull moſt parte deſcendynge borne lowe vyle ſtocke lynage whyles taken ſtate dygnyte pope knowynge ſkylled ſeculer gouernaunce ignoraunte orderynge ryches beynge alſo vndyſcrete perſones lately made ryche nowe made become importable intollerable vnto chryſten people ¶ moreouer beleuynge laufull ſoeuer luſte reaſon fulnes powre whiche chalenge dewe vnto ſelues haue made make certayne oligarchicall ordynacyons called decretalles whiche decree ſuche thynges obſerued kepte ſuppoſe agreynge vnto temporall profyte ſelues theyr clarkes laye men exempcion wherof haue ſpoken though great preiudyce prynces chryſten men ſoeuer dyſobedyent vnto theſe decretalles ſtryke haue ſayde theyr ſentence curſe outher mouthe el wrytynge yea oh ſhame ſhames ouer ſome haue braſt forth laſte ſo great madnes theſe theyr decretalles myght gyue moche auctoryte vnto kynge emperoure rome dothe vii electours yet let man thynke yt ſpeke thus contempte electours mockynge deryſyon hym wolde depryue auctoryte dewe vnto ignoraunte vertue nature eleccyon cauſe powre auctoryte ſayde eleccyon dothe conſyſte reſte bygger parte ought electe thoſe emperoure effecte therof neyther ought neyther maye depende hange vpon wyll one man alone yf manyfeſtlye preiudyce vnto naye rather ſpeake truely dothe anulle theyr offyce vtterlye ſayde theyr auctoryte regale auctoryte romaynes gyuen vnto man agayne without theyr conſente determynacion dothe aſcrybe confyrmacyon emperour elected vnto hym ſelfe ſaye without ſayd confyrmacion man emperour ought called kynge emperoure ought mynyſtre thynges appertaynynge emperoure none thynge prohybyte perpetually creacyon promocyon ſayd prynce emperoure elles bryng ſayd empyre holly ſeruytude bondage byſſhop rome byſſhop rome yf lyſte wyl neuer approue confyrme man elected kynge emperour romaynes aſmoch affyrmeth hym ſelfe ſuperyoure vnto men thynge vnder colledge ſyngulare perſone nowe ſhall neuer lyſte wyllynge approue confyrme man elected becauſe afore doth approue hym whiche elected kynge emperoure wyll requyre hym promyſes othes amonge wyll requyre ye othe wherby emperour ſhall ſaye expreſſe hym ſelfe ſubiecte vnto ſayd byſſhop fealtye temporall coactyue iuryſdyccyon wyll requyre alſo vnlawfull vniuſte occupacyons certayne prouynces kepte mayntayned vnto hym ſelfe ſayd elected emperoure thynge wyll requyre promyſed confyrmed othe ſayd elected emperoure vnlawfull promyſes othes beynge poſſyble made neyther holden kepte vnlaufull othes ye emperours ye byſſhop rome made ſauynge conſcience emperours maieſtie lawfull othe gyuen made creacyon cōſerue mayntayne lyberties empyre neuer man beynge elected emperour wyll gyue make byſſhop rome byſſhop excepte ſofte cowardlye woman alſo manyfeſtlye periured ſwerynge promyſynge ſuche maner thynges wherfore none emperours elected ſhall euer created emperour romaynes ſhall deſerue name emperoure yf regall emperyall auctoryte perſones elected doth hange byſſhop rome longe ſayde byſſhoppe maye lette prohybyte thoughe doth vniuſtlye ſekynge thoſe thynges whiche appertayne hym queſtyon wyll let bothe wordes alſo workes dedes ſo longe may yet foloweth alſo greuous preiudyce vntollerable hurte theſe aforeſayde yt prynces trybutes ſeruycꝭ whiche hathe ben wonte done ſame vnto emperours rome thynges whiche ſayd byſſhop ſhall lyſte fayne dewe vnto hym ſelfe beyonde cuſtome fulnes powre whiche ſayth openlye belonge vnto hym ſelfe foloweth alſo collacyon gyuynge pryncedomes fee lybertyes whiche emperour rome may gyue defaulte hayres male reaſon cauſe dothe lykewyſe appertayne auctoryte ſayde byſſhop emperyall ſeate beynge vacaunte yea foloweth moreouer whiche moſte preiudycyall moſte greuouſe thynge whan emperyall ſee vacaunte whiche powre dylygence byſſhops rome ſhall perpetually vacaunte prynces colledgies cōmunyties ſyngulare perſones whiche ſubiectes empyre rome contendynge ſtryuynge cyuyly one reaſon appellacyons cōmynge betwene throughe complayntes made brought vnto courte byſſhop rome well reall perſonall ſhall compelled come courte ſayd byſſhop cytacyons abyde cyuyle tēporal iudgement prynce cōmunyte iudge beynge ſubiecte emperour rome ſhall able put ſentēce reaſon perſons condempned ſhall alwayes ſtoppe ſuche execucyon appele temporall ſentences vnto courte rome yf ſubiecte empyre rome wyll obeye ſayde byſſhop vnder hym aforeſayde thynges bounde ſayde byſſhoppe ſhal contynuallye without ceaſynge malycious frowarde enforcemēt perſue ſentēcꝭ called curſynges blaſphemyes excōmunycacyons hereſyes interdyccyons laſte beynge depryued loſynge theyr temporall goodes makynge ſuche maner temporalles cōmune grauntynge ſoeuer ſhall able maner waye plucke awaye grauntynge dothe purſue ſuche perſones theyr ſubiectes adherentes whiche alſo whatſoeuer meane kyll ſlee falſe dyſceyptfull pardon maner pardon ſynne payne alſo abſoluynge thoughe heretycally ſubiectes theyr othes outher afore gyuen afterwardes gyuen vnto abſolucions ſayd prynces yf byſſhop rome pretēdynge wonted maner cure loue people ſhall ſaye therfore appertayneth vnto obieccion hym ſelfe confyrme alowe eleccyon emperoure rome leſte peraduenture heretyke myght clyme vp vnto emperyall dygnyte whiche reaſon therof wolde verye moche hurte cōmunyte chryſten people verely anſwere made vnto hym conuenyentlye ſayd eleccion nedeth anſwere therfore alowed hym aſmoche ſame eleccyon celebrated made iii ſolempne archebyſſhops chryſtendom whiche eche one hath taken great auctoryte preeſthode epyſcopall powre chryſte hathe byſſhop rome alſo iiii ſeculare chryſten prynces whome whan aforeſayde relygyous paſtours prelate agree togyther eleccyon aforeſayde emperoure made perfyte lyke trewe theſe vii wyll ſo erre moued peruerſe intencyon corrupte affeccyon dothe wyll byſſhoppe rome alone hym ſelfe whiche thynketh ſuppoſeth maye ryght leaue vnto owne iudgement alone ye reaſon fulnes powre vnaccordyngely dothe aſcrybe vnto hym ſelfe ſo myghte pleaſure iudge whome ſoeuer lyſte heretyke ſo depryue hym ryght eleccyon reaſon wherof offyce prynces electours ſhulde made voyde creacion promotynge hym elected ſhulde alwayes prohybyted letted cauſes aforeſayde yet caſe put accordynge mynde aduerſarye emperoure rome outher afore eleccyon hathe falen doth fall hereſye prynces electours knowledge therof yet ſayde iudgement correccyon hym dothe wyſe therfore appertayne byſſhop rome moreouer demaunded yet creature creaturꝭ lyuyng ablynge kynges dothe belonge alſo theyr ſayd iudgemente powre approbacyon dare ſuertye intende alſo thoughe dare yet attempte ſet vpon wayte mete conuenyent tyme therfore wherof alſo peraduenture ſhall ſpeake ſomwhat theſe ſayde falſe ſuppoſycions laſt certayne one called pope rome entrynge way erroure iniquyte al ſtudye inforcementes letteth prohybyteth noble ludouyke deſcendynge duke bauarye elecced kynge romaynes procede vnto quyete poſſeſſyon hyghe emperyall dygnyte ſayd ludouyke bothe worde alſo dede kylleth deſtroyeth cauſe ſuppoſycions aforeſayde byſſhop albeit hathe yet ben approued confyrmed wordes wrytynges haue euydentlye ſhewed neyther neadeth confyrmed yet withſtā dynge tyme eleccion made publyſſhed electours hyther contynuallye hathe cauſed dothe cauſe hym ſelfe wryten named kynge romaynes dede accordynge trouth hathe ben alſo dothe admynyſtre thynges belongynge ſayd kynge emperoure poyntes may alſo bounde ryght wherfore accordynge tale eſope worthy marked well agreynge purpoſe ſerpent byſſhoppe rome nowe albeit hathe ben exalted releued auaunced predeceſſours ſayd ludouyke predeceſſours great pouertye vylenes oppreſſyon rebuke perſecucyon vnto abundaunce temporall goodes hyghe dygnyte honoure powre tranquyllite yet lyke vnkynde perſone one forgotten aforeſayde benefytes hathe lyfted vp hym ſelfe agaynſt aforeſayd ludouyke fyrſte lewde wonte maner ſpyttynge many wordes rebuke dyſworſhyp irreuerence agaynſt ſayd prynce yet offrynge venome poyſone vnder apperaunce hony pretendeth olde crafte deceypte coloure apparaunce vertue charyte ſaythe certayne epyſtles whiche calleth decree wryteth ſpeaketh ſuche thynges ende myght brynge agayne ſayd ludouyke bypathe erroure vnto ryghte waye pathe truthe helthe regardynge hym ſelfe whiche ſpeaketh neyther ſpeaketh neyther whome ſpeaketh byſſhop beynge waye truth parteles equyte may ſay cōuenyently verely truly chryſte texte vii mathewe viii luke ſeeſt thou ſtrawe iye thy brother doſt ſe bealme thyne owne iye ſayſt thou thy brother brother ſuffre caſte ſtrawe thyne iye haſte bealme thyne owne iye thou hypocryte fyrſte caſte bealme thyne owne iye ſhalte thou ſe caſte ſtrawe thy brother iye good tree whiche bryngeth forth euylfruyte neyther euyll tree bryngyng forth good fruyte euery tree knowen owne fruyte dothe hypocryte moſt euyltree brynge euery fruytes malyce ſeducyon dyſcorde ſencyble knowen men dothe go aboute defame vertuous man innocent catholyke prayſed men wordes ignomine ſlaundre vnder falſe apperaunce coloure deuocyon charyte let hym fyrſte caſte owne mynde beynge ful darkenes blynde bealme wyt moſt great ignoraunce erroure owne lewde affeccyon beynge maner oftynate durated let hym caſte waye malyce furyous woodnes ſhall able ſe ſmall faultes men maye exortacions monycyons metelye conuenyentlye caſte men afterwarde aforeſayd byſſhop whiche vnder ſuch deceyptfull fayned wordes dothe intende amendment man cyuyle deathe deſtruccyon cōmune weale hathe powred forthe ſpredde abrode agaynſt aforeſayde moſte chryſten prynce venomes poyſons cyuyle lyfe whiche hathe ſuppoſed moſte deadlye vnto hym hathe excōmunycated hym thoſe pertyculerly cleue vnto hym hath alſo forbydden exercyſe dyuyne ſeruyce vnto cōmunyties chryſten men whiche gyue aboute gyue helpe counſayle fauour vnto ſame prynce beynge kynge romaynes lytle nothynge markyng regardynge counſayle ſaynt ambroſe boke whiche intytled de ſacerdotali dignitate ambroſe treatynge texte paule thyrde chapytre fyrſte epyſtle timothe yf man deſyreth preeſthode c amonge thynges viii chapytre ſayde booke ſayth thus brawler ſaye let preeſte louſe tonge raylynge euyll wordes lefte ſame tonge whiche gyueth prayſes god offereth vp deuyne ſeruyce brynge forth venome poyſon braulynge ſtryfe ſemely bothe benedyccyon maledyccyon ſhulde yſſue preeſtes mouthe agayne lefte ſame tonge whiche god lawded man maye deſprayſed euyll ſpoken maye brynge forthe bothe ſwete water bytter water one fountayne ſprynge concluſyon peraduenture ſhall ſende forthe prycke ſtynge malyce whiche ſuppoſeth moſt vtter extreme noyenge dyſtroyenge ſuppoſynge faſten vpon ſayde prynce wytte certayne blaſphemye called hym ſentence thoughe verye fruytes haue cō med proceded theſe many hūdred yeres ye ſeat rome holy father mayntayned o• holy father dede maye called madnes whiche hathe pronounced aforeſayde prynce dothe cleue vnto hym dothe obeye hym fauoure hym kynge romaynes heretykes enemyes rebellyons vnto churche whiche ſentence hathe depryued berefte ryght theyr temporalles bothe moueables vnmoueables makynge ſayde temporalles cōmune aforeſayde ſentence vnworthelye ſo called grauntynge alſo ſoeuer lyſt entre vpon wynne get vyolence ſpreadynge abrode prouynces wordes elles wrytynges parchement hym ſelfe el certayne falſe preacher maye done lawfullye agayne condempnynge deathe grauntynge remyſſyon forgyuenes al ſynnes paynes punyſſhementes crymes vnto thoſe kylle inuade eccleſyaſtycall offyces alſo ſpendeth therto eccleſyaſtycall temporalles called benefyces treaſures money churche maye rayſe vp men enuye rebellyon warre dyſcorde agayne ſayd prynce dothe albeit dothe nothynge belonge auctoryte gyue forthe ſentence forſayde thynges haue euydentlye declared beſyde theſe horryble malygnytes aforeſayde exercyſeth newe kynde wyckednes malyce whiche ſemeth manyfeſtlye ſmell hereſye rayſeth vp rebellyon agaynſt ſayde catholyke prynce owne ſubiectes leyge people aſſoylynge deuyllyſſhe ſayenges wrytynges calleth al apoſtolycall wryttes othes fidelyte whiche ben verye eccleſiaſticall offyces benefyces ¶ worke apoſtolyke diabolycall dede euydent accordynge ſayde byſſhoppe complyces ordynatours conſenters executers worde wrytynge dede beynge blynde couytouſnes pryde ambicyon fylled moſte great iniquyte euydent men guydes leader gyue credence vnto folowe worke dede aforeſayde ſayenges wrytynges vnto fallynge goynge downe heedlynge dyche pytte deadly ſynnes fyrſte manyfeſt open periurye afterwardes treaſon iniurye open playne men conſequentlye cauſeth fall rauyne robbrye manſlaughter maner kyndes myſcheuous ſynnes whiche dyenge without repentaunce beynge begyled moſte holy father mynyſters yet excuſed god theyr groſſe ignoraunce caſte downe heedlonge drowned hell wytte pytte perpetuall dampned perſones ought vndoubted euery man hathe reaſon able vſe neyther byſſhoppe rome neyther preeſte may aſſoyle man ſuche maner lawfull othe outher gyuen made el promyſed nowe euydent euery man wyll ſtande owne conſcyence whiche troubled ſynyſtre croked affeccyon cauſe whiche byſſhoppe rome pretendeth agaynſt ye deuoute prynce lewes agaynſt prynce lyke caſe reſonable vnreſonable vndyſcrete vniuſt wherfore gydynge doctryne exhortacyon byſſhoppe mynyſters ſuch thynges eſchewed auoyded vtterlye deſpyſed thynge whiche leadeth bryngeth concluſyon vnto eternall deathe ſoules playnly openly contrary holſome doctryne wordes ſentence apoſtle paule cōmaundementes godes lawe neyther conſonant agreable vnto rather diſſonaunt manyfeſte repugnaunt contrarye ſayde lawe hathe ben ſhewed ſcrypture iiii v ix chapytours dyccyon agayne obeye byſſhoppe depryue theyr ſuffycyēt lyfe worlde fynallye brynge ben ſo dyſpoſed theyr mynde yf maye therto attende haue ſayde vnto eternall dyſtruccyon theyr ſoules wherfore let chryſten men dyſpyſe beware vayne precept ye apoſtle rather god ſayenge playnlye without metaphore xiii chapytre romaynes let euery ſoule ſubiecte hygh power teache openlye ſoeuer reſyſteth ye power kynge hed prynce ye deuyll yea couetous proude hyghe mynded blaſphemous perſons obedyent theyr parentes vnder worde parentes comprehendynge prynces gouernours wherfore tully de officiis fyrſte boke ſaythe prynces ben contrey parentes whoſe great benefytes bounden obedyent dyſobedyent therfore theyr parentes moche ſaye dyſobedyent prynces foloweth ſayenge paule vnkynde perſones full myſcheyfe vnfaythfull kepynge promyſe chapytre mathewe take hede ware falſe prophetes whiche come vnto apparayle ſhepe inwardlye rauenynge wolues theyr fruytes ſhall knowe apoſtle ſaythe comformablye aforeſayd counſayle precepte chryſte ſuch perſones auoyde thou ſaye beleue neyther obeye ſuche thynges ala pytuous caſe haue throughe apperaunce godlynes ſo greatlye deceyued begyled men nowe truſtynge vyolente powre whiche haue optayned gotten vnder apperaunce ſymylytude holynes partly mennes free gyfte great parte ſecrete preuy vſurpacyon nowe open vyolent vſurpacyon well auoyded eſchewed doynge vyolence perſecucyon chryſtes complyces nowe ſeme onelye agaynſt emperoure emperours ar vexed byſſhop rome ſo kynges theyr byſſhops clargye rome yet let prynces learne example ſayde emperoure whiche hathe ben ſo greatlye benefyciall byſſhoppe rome churche ſame thynges may lykelyhode chaunce vnto ſelues alſo aforeſayde byſſhoppe ſhall full buſye ſame thynges agaynſt alſo whan occaſyon ſuche aſſaulte ſhall offre ſelfe vnto hym without good affeccyon towardes euery man affyrmynge wordes wrytynges aforeſayde prynces people ſubiectes gouernaunce coactyue iuryſdyccyon becauſe fulnes powre calleth whiche vnaccordynglye aſcrybeth vnto hym ſelfe day byſſhops clargy wayte couetynge alſo deſyrynge greatly brynge effecte wayteth ſuche tymes whiche appereth ſcyſmes contencyons chryſten prynces people one rebellyon ſubiectes agaynſt theyr ſoueraygnes ruler whiche ſedycions contencions rebellyons hym ſelfe alſo procureth otherwhyles rayſed ſtyrred vp intente ſo one partes beynge dyſcorde betwene ſelues beynge weake feble beynge able reſyſte aduerſarye parte may compelled beſeche helpe ayde ſubmyt hym ſelfe domynion albeit vnder fayned face apperaunce holynes deuocyon charyte ſemeth otherwhyles defende impotēt weake perſons peraduenture wrongfully oppreſſed gyue vnto ſeculare fauour yet gyueth fauour excepte ſure afore whiche nede fauour requyre wyll content come vnder gouernaunce ſeculare domynion hopynge therof concluſyon ſuche oppreſſynge enuye eche bothe partꝭ beyng ſo varyaunce ſhall compelled come vnder domynion wherfore ſuche contencyons accyons auoyded whiche may brynge cauſe neceſſyte vnto man fauoure helpe laſte turned deſtruccyon lybertye ſeruytude thraldom receyue ſayde fauoure ¶ maner ſayd byſſhop lytle lytle crepeth ſucceſſyuely throughe kyngdoms worlde may laſt able ſubdue make ſubiecte vnto hym ſelfe empyres domynions worlde whiche thynge inceſſauntly deſyreth dareth attempte ſuche maner proceſſes many togyther one tyme abydeth vntyll ſuche cunnynge poynte practicaſyon ſence meanynge tytle fulnes powre hath preſumed take vpon hym doth expreſſely ſay forth prynces empyres ſubiecte domynyon coactyue iuryſdyccion lykewyſe ſayth empyre ye romaynes nowe ſubiecte vnto hym thoſe wolde refuſe although myght lawfully ſubiecte vnto hym doth purſue blaſphemyes lyke ſentences theſe afore mayntayned agaynſt emperour rome faythfull ſubiectes alſo vyolent armed powre euen vnto chapytre luke chryſte 6 ſayd ſpecyally vnto hym haue prayed peter thy faythe may fayle thou one beynge cōuerted confyrme ſtrengthe thy brother ſemeth folowe pryncypall paſtorall cure confyrmacyon brother wyt apoſtles chryſten men cōmytted betaken vnto ſaynt peter becauſe fyrmytie ſtedfaſtnes faythe whiche chryſt ſemeth ſpecyally haue prayed ſhuld faynt quēched neyther hym neyther ſucceſſour hym gloſe ſayth thus confyrme thy brother ſeynge haue made cheyfe pryncypall apoſtles vnderſtanded onelye apoſtles whiche tyme ſhulde ſtrengthed peter chryſten men lytle foloweth gloſe repentaunce obtayned wyt peter pryncypall byſſhop ye worlde ¶ agayn 7 ſame ſhewed xxi chapytre iohn̄ chryſte ſayde ſeuerally hym fede ſhepe fede lambes fede ſhepe reherſynge ſame worde thryes appereth therfore ſhall contynewe remayne vntyl come folowe thou ſaynt auguſtyne ſayth churche knoweth two lyues ſhewed vnto ſelfe god aboue whiche one faythe beleue hope lyfe wytte faythe ſygnyfyed marked forth peter apoſtle becauſe prymacye pryncypalyte apoſtleſhyp agayne theophilus ſame place ſaythe thus hathe inſtytuted hym prelacye chryſten people chryſoſtome ſaythe thus yf man wyl ſay aſke queſtyon howe maner toke iames vnto hym ſelfe epyſcopall ſeate ieruſalem truely wyll ſaye becauſe hathe introniſated ſtalled peter mayſter whole worlde ſame chryſoſtome ſaythe afterwardes hym wytte peter alſo ouerſyght gouernaunce prelacye brother hathe ben cōmytted betaken agayne ſame chriſoſtome ſayth therfore becauſe lorde ſhewed ſayde great thynges vnto hym wyt peter commytted betaken hym whole worlde agayne theophilus vpon texte yf wyll remayne ſaythe thus dymytte ſende nowe offyce ouerſeer byſſhopryche whole worlde folowe thou moreouer yf chryſte inſtytuted heed churche abſence ſhulde haue lefte heedles without heed ſhulde ſeme haue ordered accordynge better beſte dyſpoſycyon nowe beleued hathe lefte ordred dyſpoſed beſt wyſe maner wherfore holden hathe inſtytute made heed ſayd churche none conuenyent heed peter wherfore may concluded ſaynt peter ſuperyoure apoſtles auctoryte īmedyate inſtytucyon ordynacyon chryſte ¶ agayne maye proue ſame thynge kynde ſhewynge ſaynt paule 8 egall ſaynt hereafter foloweth ¶ therfore make anſwere fyrſt vnto y• obiecciōs made laſte chapytre afore anſwere made fyrſt obieccyon chapytre laſt paſte gone reaſoned yt byſſhops greatter eſſencial inſeperable multytude chryſten people ſuche maner eleccyon myght celebrated thoughe ben yet coulde haue yet ben done ſo cōuenyently multitude chryſt hym ſelfe whiche cauſe apoſtles alſo paſſyon reſurreccyon therfore yf ſhall haue ſeculer iudgementes ordeyne ſette iudges whiche contemptyble churche ſaye rebuke none ſo wyſe man amonge whiche maye gyue iudgement betwene brother brother dothe one brother contende ſtryue brother iudgement afore infydels heathen iudges whiche texte apoſtle gloſe expoundynge mynde ambroſe auguſtyne gregorye ſaythe wyſe lyke maner hath repreued pleaded cauſes ſtroue iudgement afore infydels deſpyſynge ſmally regardynge chryſten men euen ſo nowe rebuketh becauſe made contēptyble perſones iudges althought chryſten therfore ſaythe yf ſhall haue ſeculer iudgementes becauſe ſuche iudgementes rather deſpyſed yf haue ſuche iudgementes ordayne ſette gyue iudgement thoſe contemptyble ſaye vndyſcrete vyle perſones whiche churche ſaye thus haue done reaſon wherof brother myghte compelled haue recourſe agayn •• vnto infydels hethen iudges apoſtle repreueth rebuketh ſpeakynge ironycallye ſaye meanynge contrarye wordes dothe ſounde becauſe ſemely conuenyent ſhulde ſo therofre ſayth ſpeake ſhamefaſtnes reuerence ſaye cōmaunde ſpeake ſhulde aſſhamed oughte aſhamed one man amonge ſo wyſe able iudge betwene brother brother muſt nedelye make fooles iudges yet theſe fooles made iudges rather ſhulde go heathen iudges yf wante wyſe men amonge ſaye ſo wyſe man amonge dothe one brother ſtryue brother iudgement whiche euyll thynge yea afore heathen iudges worſe thynge elles thus therfore yf ſhall haue ſeculer iudgementes c becauſe apoſtle ſayd myght iudge theſe leaſte ſmaleſt thynges therfore doth nowe determyne ordayned appoynted iudges determynynge
